-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694"><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:0">`**`</span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:1">, </span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:2">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:3">, </span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:4">`/`</span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:5"> and </span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:6">`%`</span><span data-offset-key="0fdd324a0db549f99b7239c995151694:7"> have higher precedence, or priority.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="34797288a7de4b6ba9172df69a0581e4"><span data-offset-key="34797288a7de4b6ba9172df69a0581e4:0">`+`</span><span data-offset-key="34797288a7de4b6ba9172df69a0581e4:1"> and </span><span data-offset-key="34797288a7de4b6ba9172df69a0581e4:2">`-`</span><span data-offset-key="34797288a7de4b6ba9172df69a0581e4:3"> have a lower precedence.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6"><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:0">Sub-expressions involving operators from {</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:3">`/`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:5">`%`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:6">, </span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:7">`**`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:8">} are evaluated before those involving operators from {</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:9">`+`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:10">, </span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:11">`-`</span><span data-offset-key="edf352f423414938b8b66e7b85f34ae6:12">}</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1"><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:0">Let’s try another small puzzle on precedence, with </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:1">`5 - 2 * 2`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:2">. What would be the result of this? Will it be </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:3">`6`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:4">, or </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:5">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:6">? It’s </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:7">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:8">, because </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:9">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:10"> has a higher precedence than </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:11">`-`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:12">. Thus </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:13">`2 * 2`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:14"> is </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:15">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:16">, and </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:17">`5 - 4`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:18"> gives us </span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:19">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="eac2efb7f7f74c52930b1bfae9bf90e1:20">.</span></span></span>

        >>> 5 - 2 * 2    1

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0"><span data-offset-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0:0">Let’s say we want to execute </span><span data-offset-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0:1">`5 - 2`</span><span data-offset-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0:2">, to give an output of </span><span data-offset-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0:3">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="df976c024a234891ad556d34486e53f0:4">. How do we change the operator precedence?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d6268d6f49094fafb18b753969b3b051"><span data-offset-key="d6268d6f49094fafb18b753969b3b051:0">You cannot really change the precedence, but you can add parentheses to group sub-expressions differently.</span></span></span>

        >>> (5 - 2) * 2    6    >>> 5 - ( 2 * 2 )    1

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020"><span data-offset-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020:0">Parentheses have the highest precedence in Python, and can be used to override operator precedence. </span><span data-offset-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020:1">`(5 - 2)`</span><span data-offset-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020:2"> gets calculated first, and the final result of the expression is </span><span data-offset-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020:3">`6`</span><span data-offset-key="29d8c60bffb6497f9129c5e426be0020:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c122d2d3bdf043eb8169341295f25310"><span data-offset-key="c122d2d3bdf043eb8169341295f25310:0">A positive thing about using parentheses is, that it makes expressions more readable. So even in situations such as </span><span data-offset-key="c122d2d3bdf043eb8169341295f25310:1">`5 - 2 * 2`</span><span data-offset-key="c122d2d3bdf043eb8169341295f25310:2">, where we know the result according to precedence, adding parentheses is good.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4086924eefc44c53ac9069ab0bf1635b"><span data-offset-key="4086924eefc44c53ac9069ab0bf1635b:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e1b7b18c725d4358bb01d7795b148e69"><span data-offset-key="e1b7b18c725d4358bb01d7795b148e69:0">In this step, we went about solving a few puzzles about expressions, touching concepts such as:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4d1cf3a3c1ec40bab55cfbd4a47db5cd"><span data-offset-key="4d1cf3a3c1ec40bab55cfbd4a47db5cd:0">`SyntaxError`</span><span data-offset-key="4d1cf3a3c1ec40bab55cfbd4a47db5cd:1"> for incorrect operators</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="395f4810ccb9421fb43cf17105ac0e21"><span data-offset-key="395f4810ccb9421fb43cf17105ac0e21:0">White-space in expressions</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="96c28a270c0c49208b8ecf395fff79a3"><span data-offset-key="96c28a270c0c49208b8ecf395fff79a3:0">Floating Point division by default</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="99a1ab751899422e946a3f48454b014d"><span data-offset-key="99a1ab751899422e946a3f48454b014d:0">Operator Precedence</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a4e8820e08ee473a8108f46b52e5a1e6"><span data-offset-key="a4e8820e08ee473a8108f46b52e5a1e6:0">Using parentheses</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="59e4cb50c2014947a85b608f7ff7aa25"><span data-offset-key="59e4cb50c2014947a85b608f7ff7aa25:0">Step 06: Printing Text</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b479112640f9466f9a0fa28fd5ca50b6"><span data-offset-key="b479112640f9466f9a0fa28fd5ca50b6:0">In the previous step, we learned how to use expressions to compute values. In this step, let’s see how we can actually print multiplication table entries, that are readable by the user.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0df8c38af6df4251bd5c9f380dc885f7"><span data-offset-key="0df8c38af6df4251bd5c9f380dc885f7:0">**Snippet-01: Printing Text**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6"><span data-offset-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6:0">How do we go about printing a complete multiplication table entry? We want to print text such as </span><span data-offset-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6:1">`5 * 6 = 30`</span><span data-offset-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6:2"> . But trying to do so, as we know it, gives us a </span><span data-offset-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6:3">`SyntaxError`</span><span data-offset-key="5ac73c09c3024d7585d427c1cf4af5e6:4">. Clearly, there is a different way to print text, as compared to an expression.</span></span></span>

        >>> 5 * 6 = 30      File "<stdin>", line 1    SyntaxError: can't assign to operator

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="086d862464e24bc7b44e5f286f5a8a26"><span data-offset-key="086d862464e24bc7b44e5f286f5a8a26:0">Let’s first try to print a simple piece of text, </span><span data-offset-key="086d862464e24bc7b44e5f286f5a8a26:1">`Hello`</span><span data-offset-key="086d862464e24bc7b44e5f286f5a8a26:2">. Typing in this piece of code directly on Python Shell also gives us an error.</span></span></span>

        >>> Hello    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    NameError: name 'Hello' is not defined

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="68d142e1f6e9432a90b277b56c1ed1c9"><span data-offset-key="68d142e1f6e9432a90b277b56c1ed1c9:0">Only expressions work that way, and </span><span data-offset-key="68d142e1f6e9432a90b277b56c1ed1c9:1">`Hello`</span><span data-offset-key="68d142e1f6e9432a90b277b56c1ed1c9:2"> is not really an expression.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a"><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:0">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:1"> is typically called a </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:2">**string**</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:3">, and represents the text of letters </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:4">`'H'`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:5">, </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:6">`'e'`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:7">, </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:8">`'l'`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:9">, </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:10">`'l'`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:11">, </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:12">`'o'`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:13">. </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:14">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:15"> is hence different from the number </span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:16">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="6360c979f5f64e3b8eead2bd9689be5a:17">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e"><span data-offset-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e:0">There are a number of in-built functions in Python to help print strings. One of these is the </span><span data-offset-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e:2"> function. Can you just say </span><span data-offset-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e:3">`print Hello`</span><span data-offset-key="f746428c011e433bb7419ac802b8a05e:4">?</span></span></span>

        >>> print Hello      File "<stdin>", line 1        print Hello                  ^    SyntaxError: Missing parentheses in call to 'print'. Did you mean print(Hello)?

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1ef453df3c2349bc8dc5cc1cf550aefc"><span data-offset-key="1ef453df3c2349bc8dc5cc1cf550aefc:0">The Python compiler gives you an error, that says “missing parentheses”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ee06d26fba3549b7981641ac7717115b"><span data-offset-key="ee06d26fba3549b7981641ac7717115b:0">Will </span><span data-offset-key="ee06d26fba3549b7981641ac7717115b:1">`print(Hello)`</span><span data-offset-key="ee06d26fba3549b7981641ac7717115b:2"> work?</span></span></span>

        >>> print (Hello)    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    NameError: name 'Hello' is not defined

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7d1e7c4e2fa74dedbb4b517584d63cef"><span data-offset-key="7d1e7c4e2fa74dedbb4b517584d63cef:0">Nope! Again, this one failed because you need to indicate that </span><span data-offset-key="7d1e7c4e2fa74dedbb4b517584d63cef:1">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="7d1e7c4e2fa74dedbb4b517584d63cef:2"> is a string.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0a598de1a9df4a169fd95602577841fc"><span data-offset-key="0a598de1a9df4a169fd95602577841fc:0">How do I indicate that </span><span data-offset-key="0a598de1a9df4a169fd95602577841fc:1">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="0a598de1a9df4a169fd95602577841fc:2"> is a string? By putting it within double quotes.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="88bd7ebcdb1642878205f3e47fb1e3c2"><span data-offset-key="88bd7ebcdb1642878205f3e47fb1e3c2:0">Let’s try </span><span data-offset-key="88bd7ebcdb1642878205f3e47fb1e3c2:1">`print ("Hello")`</span></span></span>

        >>> print ("Hello")    Hello    >>> print("Hello")    Hello

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5"><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:0">`print("Hello")`</span><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:1"> finally results in </span><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:2">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:3"> being printed out. To be able to print </span><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:4">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="72803c07dc7344bf83aefb7cc68440a5:5">, the things we need to do are:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e6d1a099df2d4cc48bead43ee0b44d04"><span data-offset-key="e6d1a099df2d4cc48bead43ee0b44d04:0">Typing the method name print ,</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a057e9c604b04e66a9e297f5fed8c43f"><span data-offset-key="a057e9c604b04e66a9e297f5fed8c43f:0">open parentheses ( ,</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5165061bb3f34a19ae9f652318d36218"><span data-offset-key="5165061bb3f34a19ae9f652318d36218:0">Followed by a double quote " ,</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="03ed75d5fb1245fd907959ccfc53e49b"><span data-offset-key="03ed75d5fb1245fd907959ccfc53e49b:0">The text Hello,</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d6ac8a1791df40cfa1f03d72a867107d"><span data-offset-key="d6ac8a1791df40cfa1f03d72a867107d:0">and another double quote " ,</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eab847d0a3404d2aa82415651b80585c"><span data-offset-key="eab847d0a3404d2aa82415651b80585c:0">finished off with a closed parentheses ).</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8"><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:0">What we have written here is called a </span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:1">**statement**</span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:2">, a simple piece of code to execute. As part of this statement, we are </span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:3">**calling**</span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:4"> a </span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:5">**function**</span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:6">, named </span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:7">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="11d480babfa64d7cbeebacf387bb10c8:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cc823f87809c444d92c85d8049add8da"><span data-offset-key="cc823f87809c444d92c85d8049add8da:0">What exactly are we trying to print?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6"><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:0">The text </span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:1">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:2">, which is called a </span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:3">**parameter**</span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:4"> or </span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:5">**argument**</span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:6">, to </span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:7">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="1b9e7c3fc8274ef4b34617b2fa7bdaf6:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e"><span data-offset-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e:0">Now let’s get back to what we wanted to do, which is to print </span><span data-offset-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e:1">`5 * 6 = 30`</span><span data-offset-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e:2">. The most basic version would be something of this kind, </span><span data-offset-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e:3">`print("5 * 6 = 30")`</span><span data-offset-key="2ecd0b7d81334785891139739b62e48e:4">. Here, we are passing the entire value in the form of a string.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("5 * 6 = 30")    5 * 6 = 30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519"><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:0">This prints the text on the console, as-is. The thing you need to understand here is, we aren’t really calculating </span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:1">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:2"> using the formula </span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:3">`5 * 6`</span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:4">, but directly putting text </span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:5">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:6"> in here. That’s called </span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:7">**hard-coding**</span><span data-offset-key="4066b03787ee4b52b14159e0c3a3d519:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f2d52153694a42aead428295c3e66f9c"><span data-offset-key="f2d52153694a42aead428295c3e66f9c:0">In a later step, we will look at how to actually calculate the value and pass it in.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e208275c1bfd432d9b647347a68700b8"><span data-offset-key="e208275c1bfd432d9b647347a68700b8:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2ca0729197734151bf4883612ccbe32c"><span data-offset-key="2ca0729197734151bf4883612ccbe32c:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c1af5af6b978407da73710dc31c004bf"><span data-offset-key="c1af5af6b978407da73710dc31c004bf:0">Understood that displaying text on the console is not the same as printing an expression value</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="765614e1b0ec49739f3544d3a1f7a868"><span data-offset-key="765614e1b0ec49739f3544d3a1f7a868:0">Learned about the </span><span data-offset-key="765614e1b0ec49739f3544d3a1f7a868:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="765614e1b0ec49739f3544d3a1f7a868:2"> function, that is used to print text in Python.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="231697ef0ce3496d96acfa4813d83af1"><span data-offset-key="231697ef0ce3496d96acfa4813d83af1:0">Found a way to print the text </span><span data-offset-key="231697ef0ce3496d96acfa4813d83af1:1">`"5 * 6 = 30"`</span><span data-offset-key="231697ef0ce3496d96acfa4813d83af1:2"> on the console, by hard-coding values in a string</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d3aec2afac664911bcf2a27e16d32974"><span data-offset-key="d3aec2afac664911bcf2a27e16d32974:0">Step 07: Puzzles On Utility Methods, And Strings</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc"><span data-offset-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc:0">In the previous step, we learned how to print </span><span data-offset-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc:1">`5 * 6 = 30`</span><span data-offset-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc:2">. It was not a perfect solution, because we hard-coded everything. we used an in-built function named </span><span data-offset-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc:3">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="dac98891fe314127a2b2e7801e6f61cc:4">, passed a string to it, and invoked the method.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3e4a8fe0ee374e3ead78ef2440a2d094"><span data-offset-key="3e4a8fe0ee374e3ead78ef2440a2d094:0">In this step, let’s look at a number of puzzles related to in-built methods, their parameters, and strings in general.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="624046b747964148b8bb562315c5404f"><span data-offset-key="624046b747964148b8bb562315c5404f:0">For example, let’s do </span><span data-offset-key="624046b747964148b8bb562315c5404f:1">`print("5 * 6")`</span><span data-offset-key="624046b747964148b8bb562315c5404f:2">, as in the previous step. What does this code result in?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("5*6")    5*6    >>> print('5*6')    5*6

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e92bd25657db4b64854a9785ea2d42b7"><span data-offset-key="e92bd25657db4b64854a9785ea2d42b7:0">It just prints the string </span><span data-offset-key="e92bd25657db4b64854a9785ea2d42b7:1">`"5 * 6"`</span><span data-offset-key="e92bd25657db4b64854a9785ea2d42b7:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b8311bd0ccbb425a96c0e8419435b20f"><span data-offset-key="b8311bd0ccbb425a96c0e8419435b20f:0">Let’s say we try the code </span><span data-offset-key="b8311bd0ccbb425a96c0e8419435b20f:1">`print(5 * 6)`</span><span data-offset-key="b8311bd0ccbb425a96c0e8419435b20f:2">,</span></span></span>

        >>> print(5*6)    30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1"><span data-offset-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1:0">Without the double quotes, </span><span data-offset-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1:1">`5 * 6`</span><span data-offset-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1:2"> is an expression. What will be the output? </span><span data-offset-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1:3">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="4f47e29ff910494d995e8049d51ebcc1:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d2f29e595d854500a51abcc4903f6250"><span data-offset-key="d2f29e595d854500a51abcc4903f6250:0">If you call </span><span data-offset-key="d2f29e595d854500a51abcc4903f6250:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="d2f29e595d854500a51abcc4903f6250:2"> with an expression argument, it prints the value of the expression. However, when we pass something within double quotes, it becomes a piece of text, printed as-is.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0"><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:0">An interesting thing to note is, that in Python you can use either double-quotes (</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:1">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:3">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:4">), or single-quotes (</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:5">`'`</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:7">`'`</span><span data-offset-key="26fafe72ba3e422a8a26beba0231a5d0:8">) with text values.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ad48d1efd9b34f758793cece216ebfbf"><span data-offset-key="ad48d1efd9b34f758793cece216ebfbf:0">Let’s look at a few other in-built methods within Python.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f"><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:0">Consider </span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:1">`abs()`</span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:2"> (which stands for absolute value), a method that accepts a numeric value. You can use </span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:3">`abs(10.5)`</span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:4">, passing </span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:5">`10.5`</span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:6"> as a value to it, and it prints the absolute value of </span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:7">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="d337ba298db0493d90fd3ed150354d8f:8">.</span></span></span>

        >>> abs 10.5      File "<stdin>", line 1        abs 10.5               ^    SyntaxError: invalid syntax    >>> abs(10.5)    10.5

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ddac9ab2853d495c9f45ae29a5f552e5"><span data-offset-key="ddac9ab2853d495c9f45ae29a5f552e5:0">If you pass in a string value, will it work? It complains, “</span><span data-offset-key="ddac9ab2853d495c9f45ae29a5f552e5:1">`abs()`</span><span data-offset-key="ddac9ab2853d495c9f45ae29a5f552e5:2"> function will not work with a string, it only works with numeric values”.</span></span></span>

        >>> abs("10.5")    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    TypeError: bad operand type for abs(): 'str'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60"><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:0">Let’s say you want to use a function that computes “to the power of”, for instance “</span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:1">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:2"> to the power of </span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:3">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:4">”. In Python, there’s an in-built function named </span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:5">`pow()`</span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:6">, which does just what we need. To </span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:7">`pow()`</span><span data-offset-key="c4436c2c1cda4f74a07cb4e0c4e9fe60:8">, you can pass two parameters and calculate the result. How do you do that?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6"><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:0">Will this work: </span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:1">`pow 2 5`</span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:2">? No, not at all. This code does not work as well: </span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:3">`pow(2 5)`</span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:4">. </span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:5">`pow(2, 5)`</span><span data-offset-key="42bb6b27e6424809a6a2c78fa5d4b2d6:6"> is the correct syntax.</span></span></span>

        >>> pow 2 5      File "<stdin>", line 1        pow 2 5            ^    SyntaxError: invalid syntax    >>> pow(2 5)      File "<stdin>", line 1        pow(2 5)              ^    SyntaxError: invalid syntax    >>> pow(2, 5)    32

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cac6153abc7e4d1a8b4dcccbcc0b26db"><span data-offset-key="cac6153abc7e4d1a8b4dcccbcc0b26db:0">You’ll see that </span><span data-offset-key="cac6153abc7e4d1a8b4dcccbcc0b26db:1">`32`</span><span data-offset-key="cac6153abc7e4d1a8b4dcccbcc0b26db:2"> is printed.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c"><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:0">Let’s see another example, “</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:1">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:2"> to the power of </span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:3">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:4">”. </span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:5">`pow(10,3)`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:6"> is the alternative to saying </span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:7">`10 ** 3`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:8">. This gives us </span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:9">`1000`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:10">, similar to how </span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:11">`pow()`</span><span data-offset-key="f04436e7f0774370b29541608af0a77c:12"> would.</span></span></span>

        >>> pow(10, 3)    1000    >>> 10 ** 3    1000

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0d82a893ea934c52aae7c1f84d98ae39"><span data-offset-key="0d82a893ea934c52aae7c1f84d98ae39:0">`max()`</span><span data-offset-key="0d82a893ea934c52aae7c1f84d98ae39:1"> returns maximum in a set of numbers.</span><span data-offset-key="0d82a893ea934c52aae7c1f84d98ae39:2">`min()`</span><span data-offset-key="0d82a893ea934c52aae7c1f84d98ae39:3"> function returns the minimum value.</span></span></span>

        >>> max(34, 45, 67)    67    >>> min(34, 45, 67)    34

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="150e5862607f44ccb372ef673b41c4fe"><span data-offset-key="150e5862607f44ccb372ef673b41c4fe:0">These are some of the in-built functions in Python, and we saw how to call the in-built functions by passing in a varied number of parameters.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a"><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:0">Python is case sensitive. So let’s say I want of calculate </span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:1">`pow(2,5)`</span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:2">. So this would give me </span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:3">`32`</span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:4">. Now, what if I say capital </span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:5">`'P'`</span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:6"> instead of small </span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:7">`'p'`</span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:8"> here? </span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:9">`Pow(2,5)`</span><span data-offset-key="1596c168b149409cafb27d6c6587169a:10"> would lead to an error.</span></span></span>

        >>> pow(2,5)    32    >>> Pow(2,5)    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    NameError: name 'Pow' is not defined

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089"><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:0">The only things not case-sensitive in Python, are string values. Earlier we saw that the code </span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:1">`print("Hello")`</span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:2"> displays the text </span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:3">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:4">. Inside a string, the text can be in any case. Hence, </span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:5">`print("hello")`</span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:6"> displays </span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:7">`"hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:8"> ,with a small </span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:9">`'h'`</span><span data-offset-key="f09b67f9b1c04919aac11c09e1728089:10">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("Hello")    Hello    >>> print("hello")    hello    >>> print("hellO")    hellO    >>> print ( "hellO" )    hellO

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c008d80806834bceadbbcaac19949c0b"><span data-offset-key="c008d80806834bceadbbcaac19949c0b:0">However inside your code, you need to be very particular about the case of function names, class names, variable names, and the like.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c60d5fc1bf514db98acadef2ef781219"><span data-offset-key="c60d5fc1bf514db98acadef2ef781219:0">In your code, whitespace does not really matter. You can add space here and here, and you would still get the same output. However, in case of strings, whitespace does matter.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a"><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:0">If we say </span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:1">`print("hellO World")`</span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:2">, it would print </span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:3">`"hellO World"`</span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:4">, with a space in between. And if you do </span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:5">`print("hellO World")`</span><span data-offset-key="b0a72bcbdb344705b7100e8bb283205a:6"> with three spaces, it would print the same. In expressions, white-space does not affect the output.</span></span></span>

        >>> print ( "hellO World" )    hellO World    >>> print ( "hellO     World" )    hellO     World

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4"><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:0">The last thing we want to look at, is an </span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:1">**escape sequence**</span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:2">. Let’s say you want to print a double quote, </span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:3">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:4">, in the code. If we were to do this: </span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:5">`print("Hello"")`</span><span data-offset-key="3e78cc805aaf4765b0aed05e96afbaf4:6">, what would happen? The compiler says error!</span></span></span>

        >>> print("Hello"")      File "<stdin>", line 1        print("Hello"")                      ^    SyntaxError: EOL while scanning string literal

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69"><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:0">If you want to print a </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:1">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:2"> inside a string, use an escape sequence. In Python, the symbol </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:3">`'\'`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:4"> is used as an </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:5">**escape character**</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:6">. On using </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:7">`'\'`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:8"> adjacent to the </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:9">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:10">, it prints </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:11">`Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:12"> (notice the trailing </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:13">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:14">). We have used the </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:15">`'\'`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:16"> to </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:17">**escape**</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:18"> the </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:19">`"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:20">, by forming an </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:21">*escape sequence*</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:22"> </span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:23">`\"`</span><span data-offset-key="f92d5770288f4dfca7ecbfdc744cfe69:24">.</span></span></span>

    >>> print("Hello\"")Hello">>>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978"><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:0">The other reason why you would want to use a </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:1">`'\'`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:2"> is to print a </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:3">`<NEWLINE>`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:4">. If you want to print </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:5">`"Hello World"`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:6">, but with </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:7">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:8"> on one line and </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:9">`"World"`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:10"> on the next, </span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:11">`'\n'`</span><span data-offset-key="c6f6aec1416b4e3aa0f6f251c4337978:12"> is the escape sequence to use.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("Hello\nWorld")    Hello    World

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e"><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:0">The other important escape sequence is </span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:1">`'\t'`</span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:2">, which prints a </span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:3">`<TAB>`</span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:4"> in the output. When you do </span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:5">`print("Hello\tWorld")`</span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:6">, you can see the tab-space between </span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:7">`"Hello"`</span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:8"> and </span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:9">`"World"`</span><span data-offset-key="ffa6ac144c06415783ca773809a36d3e:10">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("Hello\tWorld")    Hello   World

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b"><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:0">Another useful escape sequence is </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:1">`\\`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:2"> . If you want to print a </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:3">`\`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:4"> , then use the sequence </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:5">`\\`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:6"> . You would see that it prints </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:7">`Hello\World`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:8"> . Think about what would happen if we put six </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:9">`\`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:10"> . Yes you’re right! It would print this string: </span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:11">`"\\\"`</span><span data-offset-key="99ce2ce7692a4fe3bcf3fb80387aaf9b:12"> .</span></span></span>

        >>> print("Hello\\World")    Hello\World    >>> print("Hello\\\\\\World")    Hello\\\World

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb"><span data-offset-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb:0">One of the things with Python is, it does not matter whether you use double quotes or single quotes to enclose strings. There are some interesting, and useful ways of using a combination of both, within the same string. Have a look at this call: </span><span data-offset-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb:1">`print("Hello'World")`</span><span data-offset-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb:2">, and notice the output we get. In a similar way, the following code will be accepted and run by the Python system: </span><span data-offset-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb:3">`print('Hello"World')`</span><span data-offset-key="b449ae4a8c3645f8bb3544cfd757badb:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print('Hello"')    Hello"    >>> print("Hello'World")    Hello'World    >>> print("Hello\"World")    Hello"World    >>> print("Hello\"World")    Hello"World

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3797bab2100e45e9a8dd824b43faa057"><span data-offset-key="3797bab2100e45e9a8dd824b43faa057:0">The above two examples can be used as a tip by newbie programmers when they form string literals, and want to use them in their code:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a63fb3d32c5c4e62afa3ccc5beeef20c"><span data-offset-key="a63fb3d32c5c4e62afa3ccc5beeef20c:0">If the string literal contains one or more single quotes, then you can use double quotes to enclose it.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="afa0eb5d88064b278c58c1070ababbbe"><span data-offset-key="afa0eb5d88064b278c58c1070ababbbe:0">However if the string contains one or more double quotes, then prefer to use single quotes to enclose it.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1dad30da17b24a2aa3fdc09b33d66839"><span data-offset-key="1dad30da17b24a2aa3fdc09b33d66839:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="305f0939852f44c3a3794d726dfe8f31"><span data-offset-key="305f0939852f44c3a3794d726dfe8f31:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c515b7dc1d3a473f994770944a91bfd0"><span data-offset-key="c515b7dc1d3a473f994770944a91bfd0:0">Explored a number of puzzles related to code involving:</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="99104fdda5f643209e7d5345af3b5deb"><span data-offset-key="99104fdda5f643209e7d5345af3b5deb:0">Built-in functions for numeric calculations</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="acf1b7c1861f4bfcbf69d1f6aa26eed2"><span data-offset-key="acf1b7c1861f4bfcbf69d1f6aa26eed2:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="acf1b7c1861f4bfcbf69d1f6aa26eed2:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="acf1b7c1861f4bfcbf69d1f6aa26eed2:2"> function to display expressions and strings</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8392bc82c92a4591a43ac21370c03345"><span data-offset-key="8392bc82c92a4591a43ac21370c03345:0">Covered the following aspects of the above utilities:</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8b62acb1db914249be6da266bb69dc10"><span data-offset-key="8b62acb1db914249be6da266bb69dc10:0">Case-sensitive aspects of names and strings</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82c3c1d34f674ec9b800d3f2fb1144ca"><span data-offset-key="82c3c1d34f674ec9b800d3f2fb1144ca:0">The role played by whitespace</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="94ff45921c33459795dc7430cd8c5c63"><span data-offset-key="94ff45921c33459795dc7430cd8c5c63:0">The escape character, and common escape sequences</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="72d9a3746edd4fa2bae4552416a6be1c"><span data-offset-key="72d9a3746edd4fa2bae4552416a6be1c:0">Step 08: Formatted Output With print()</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="391844e71cc34744b0cb7aa36b57ddf2"><span data-offset-key="391844e71cc34744b0cb7aa36b57ddf2:0">In the previous step, we learned how to print a hard-coded string, such as </span><span data-offset-key="391844e71cc34744b0cb7aa36b57ddf2:1">`"5 * 6 = 30"`</span><span data-offset-key="391844e71cc34744b0cb7aa36b57ddf2:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3bf87d0ba56d4817bb3bbff9e0afe057"><span data-offset-key="3bf87d0ba56d4817bb3bbff9e0afe057:0">In this step, let’s try to replace the hard-coded </span><span data-offset-key="3bf87d0ba56d4817bb3bbff9e0afe057:1">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="3bf87d0ba56d4817bb3bbff9e0afe057:2"> with a computed value.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3dea4ea697064eba826782e2453aee61"><span data-offset-key="3dea4ea697064eba826782e2453aee61:0">Let’s start with a simple scenario. Let’s say we want to place that calculated value within a string, and display it. How do we do that?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a4d8d2694892448ab398fb4bc453f751"><span data-offset-key="a4d8d2694892448ab398fb4bc453f751:0">**Snippet-01: print() Formatted Output**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="52de413f6bac41e18a8c6c3971f2f6df"><span data-offset-key="52de413f6bac41e18a8c6c3971f2f6df:0">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="52de413f6bac41e18a8c6c3971f2f6df:1"> method can be used to print formatted text.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="57ea8ddff7334f708c6784bfe5bc981a"><span data-offset-key="57ea8ddff7334f708c6784bfe5bc981a:0">Let’s see an example:</span></span></span>

        >>> print("VALUE".format(5*2))    VALUE

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8"><span data-offset-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8:0">We were expecting </span><span data-offset-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8:1">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8:2"> to be printed, but it’s actually printing </span><span data-offset-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8:3">`VALUE`</span><span data-offset-key="5375b39253044de3884d389ed8f787f8:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bafd2fd180e042b791ab928835f8959b"><span data-offset-key="bafd2fd180e042b791ab928835f8959b:0">How do we get </span><span data-offset-key="bafd2fd180e042b791ab928835f8959b:1">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="bafd2fd180e042b791ab928835f8959b:2"> to be printed then?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("VALUE {0}".format(5*2))    VALUE 10

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906"><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:0">By having an open brace </span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:1">`{`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:2">, closed brace </span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:3">`}`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:4">, and and by putting the index of the value between them. Here, the value is the first parameter, and it’s index will be </span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:5">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="cf9a7d8035c64d27b21bfdb03d9d7906:6">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d8fca872a2344c7dbd51209e925a212d"><span data-offset-key="d8fca872a2344c7dbd51209e925a212d:0">`"VALUE {0}"`</span><span data-offset-key="d8fca872a2344c7dbd51209e925a212d:1"> is what we need.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04"><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:0">Let’s take another example. Suppose to the </span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:2"> function, we pass three values: </span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:3">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:5">`20`</span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:7">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="268f8cfd011f4decbcd0d0aa54aa9f04:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bc5f7122ff124a299816543f3de9e11c"><span data-offset-key="bc5f7122ff124a299816543f3de9e11c:0">Typically when we count positions or indexes, we start from </span><span data-offset-key="bc5f7122ff124a299816543f3de9e11c:1">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="bc5f7122ff124a299816543f3de9e11c:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88"><span data-offset-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88:0">To print the first value, you need to pass in an index of </span><span data-offset-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88:1">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88:2">. To print the second value, pass an index of </span><span data-offset-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88:3">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="b3eb05f4bef74f9ea41e4474b77ffb88:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("VALUE {0}".format(10,20,30))    VALUE 10    >>> print("VALUE {1}".format(10,20,30))    VALUE 20    >>> print("VALUE {2}".format(10,20,30))    VALUE 30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e"><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:0">Now going back to our problem, we wanted to display </span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:1">`"5 * 6 = 30"`</span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:2">, but without hard-coding. Instead of </span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:3">`30`</span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:4">, we want the calculated value of </span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:5">`5 * 6`</span><span data-offset-key="e1fbaeb8e98840e9b60c143f593af66e:6">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("5 * 6 = 30".format(5,6,5*6))    5 * 6 = 30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c"><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:0">Let replace </span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:1">`"5 * 6 = 30"`</span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:2"> with </span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:3">`"5 * 6 = {2}"`</span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:4">. </span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:5">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:6"> is the index of parameter value </span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:7">`5*6`</span><span data-offset-key="7afabb7db6f245bc833e987d6135b01c:8">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("5 * 6 = {2}".format(5,6,5*6))    5 * 6 = 30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4bd76518cd874fe18068ba0e88f7eb25"><span data-offset-key="4bd76518cd874fe18068ba0e88f7eb25:0">Cool! Progress made.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde"><span data-offset-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde:0">Let’s replace </span><span data-offset-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde:1">`5 * 6`</span><span data-offset-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde:2"> with the right indices - </span><span data-offset-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde:3">`{0} * {1}`</span><span data-offset-key="e938ebae84ef46cc85cf01b45b2e4bde:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,6,5*6))    5 * 6 = 30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6"><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:0">The great thing about this, is now we can replace the values we passed to </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:2"> in the first place, without changing the indexes! So, we can display results for </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:3">`5 * 7 = 35`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:5">`5 * 8 = 40`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:6">. We are now able to print </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:7">`5 * 6 = 30`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:8">, </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:9">`5 * 7 = 35`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:10">, </span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:11">`5 * 8 = 40`</span><span data-offset-key="bcb1003eada04554a87a8c54a056d7c6:12">, and can do similar things for other table entries as well.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,7,5*7))    5 * 7 = 35    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,8,5*8))    5 * 8 = 40    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,8,5*8))    5 * 8 = 40

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dfead23d52594b5eaeb5aae2e24fe36f"><span data-offset-key="dfead23d52594b5eaeb5aae2e24fe36f:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1068552983194aefb08b0fa1be43f54c"><span data-offset-key="1068552983194aefb08b0fa1be43f54c:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d74007fc95da43af961c8b050b9a7da6"><span data-offset-key="d74007fc95da43af961c8b050b9a7da6:0">Discovered that Python provides a way to do formatted printing of string values</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7bf435cfd8ef4eebbd7da949adea8b25"><span data-offset-key="7bf435cfd8ef4eebbd7da949adea8b25:0">Looked at the </span><span data-offset-key="7bf435cfd8ef4eebbd7da949adea8b25:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="7bf435cfd8ef4eebbd7da949adea8b25:2"> function, and saw how to call it within </span><span data-offset-key="7bf435cfd8ef4eebbd7da949adea8b25:3">`print()`</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a0aaacb43a1f4c91a388d5a569f7e0f4"><span data-offset-key="a0aaacb43a1f4c91a388d5a569f7e0f4:0">Observed how we could work only with the indexes of parameters to </span><span data-offset-key="a0aaacb43a1f4c91a388d5a569f7e0f4:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="a0aaacb43a1f4c91a388d5a569f7e0f4:2">, and change the parameters we pass without changing the code</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cb2ed027a5c94b998eb4eaf855b315a7"><span data-offset-key="cb2ed027a5c94b998eb4eaf855b315a7:0">Step 09: Puzzles On format() and print()</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="885db6a95c6345648fb51c14eb81586f"><span data-offset-key="885db6a95c6345648fb51c14eb81586f:0">In this step, let’s look at a few puzzles related to the format, and the print methods.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="351b6e955a4c40c6bcf7f790e66ea24e"><span data-offset-key="351b6e955a4c40c6bcf7f790e66ea24e:0">**Snippet-01: format() And print() Puzzles**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5"><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:0">Let’s say we pass in additional values, such as: </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:1">`5 * 8`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:3">`5 * 9`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:5">`5 * 10`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:6">. However, within the call to </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:7">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:8">, we are only referring to the values at index </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:9">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:10">, index </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:11">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:12"> and index </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:13">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:14">. The values at indexes </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:15">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:16"> and </span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:17">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="7d169ab5fd8f4863a85e10c70ef5bbf5:18"> are not used at all. What would happen when we run the code?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,8,5*8,5*9,5*10))    5 * 8 = 40

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a56a7768ed09438598013010a3e5b70d"><span data-offset-key="a56a7768ed09438598013010a3e5b70d:0">Would this throw an error? No, it does not. You can see that the additional values which are passed in, are conveniently ignored.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9"><span data-offset-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9:0">Let’s say instead of passing in a value of </span><span data-offset-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9:1">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9:2">, we pass </span><span data-offset-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9:3">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="996a961ff518488dbe97b518c71679e9:4">. What would happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {4}".format(5,8,5*8,5*9,5*10))    5 * 8 = 50

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9012c05cae624b8b92cc486adc8f5d04"><span data-offset-key="9012c05cae624b8b92cc486adc8f5d04:0">`5 * 10`</span><span data-offset-key="9012c05cae624b8b92cc486adc8f5d04:1"> is the value at index </span><span data-offset-key="9012c05cae624b8b92cc486adc8f5d04:2">`4`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae"><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:0">Now let’s take a different scenario. We remove all the parameters passed to </span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:2">. However, inside the call to </span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:3">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:4">, we continue to say </span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:5">`{0} * {1} = {4}`</span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:6">. So we are trying to print the value at index </span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:7">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:8">, but are only passing two values to the function </span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:9">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="f042bd27f2bd49e48fd668c33efc30ae:10">. What do you think will happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {4}".format(5,8))    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    IndexError: tuple index out of range

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688"><span data-offset-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688:0">It says </span><span data-offset-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688:1">`IndexError`</span><span data-offset-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688:2">, which means :“you are asking me to fetch the value at index </span><span data-offset-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688:3">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="381b17e8e04047b3bbe154aa35dba688:4">, but only passing in two values. How can I do what you want?”</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490"><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:0">Let’s look at a few more things related to other data types. We try to format the following inside </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:1">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:2">: </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:3">`{0} * {1} = {2}`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:4">, and would pass in </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:5">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:6">, </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:7">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:8">, and </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:9">`2.5 * 2`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:10"> . Here, </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:11">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:12"> is an integer value, but </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:13">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:14"> is a floating point value. You can see that it prints </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:15">`2.5 * 2 = 5.0`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:16">. So this approach of formatting values with </span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:17">`print()`</span><span data-offset-key="afa50f624803495fbf55468dba97e490:18">, works also with floating point data as well.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(2.5,2,2.5*2))    2.5 * 2 = 5.0

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cd375dac45144fd7bd8d2ad1e792a0cd"><span data-offset-key="cd375dac45144fd7bd8d2ad1e792a0cd:0">Now, are there are other types of data that </span><span data-offset-key="cd375dac45144fd7bd8d2ad1e792a0cd:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="cd375dac45144fd7bd8d2ad1e792a0cd:2"> works with? Yes, strings can join the party.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="582cb4ef074248ffb97d9c4ecc4dcf27"><span data-offset-key="582cb4ef074248ffb97d9c4ecc4dcf27:0">Let’s say over here, we do: </span><span data-offset-key="582cb4ef074248ffb97d9c4ecc4dcf27:1">`print("My name is                                       {0}".format("Ranga"))`</span><span data-offset-key="582cb4ef074248ffb97d9c4ecc4dcf27:2">. What would happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("My name is {0}".format("Ranga"))    My name is Ranga

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1"><span data-offset-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1:0">Index </span><span data-offset-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1:1">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1:2"> will be replaced with the first parameter to </span><span data-offset-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1:3">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="e7599cd8acab4ecaab18425f9cb12cb1:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d9c4744f79aa4eafb5e1887353f6e296"><span data-offset-key="d9c4744f79aa4eafb5e1887353f6e296:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0e2c7f79fc2641a19665de153cc79016"><span data-offset-key="0e2c7f79fc2641a19665de153cc79016:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="333b3e54d18c4751a8107a30009b63d0"><span data-offset-key="333b3e54d18c4751a8107a30009b63d0:0">Understood the behavior when the parameters passed to </span><span data-offset-key="333b3e54d18c4751a8107a30009b63d0:1">`format()`</span><span data-offset-key="333b3e54d18c4751a8107a30009b63d0:2">:</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3c282243d2cb4f30bf67d6f8e4b549b5"><span data-offset-key="3c282243d2cb4f30bf67d6f8e4b549b5:0">Exceed the indexes accessed by </span><span data-offset-key="3c282243d2cb4f30bf67d6f8e4b549b5:1">`print()`</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="51658eb074f64c6d9e601cc8eab3a910"><span data-offset-key="51658eb074f64c6d9e601cc8eab3a910:0">Are less than the indexes accessed by </span><span data-offset-key="51658eb074f64c6d9e601cc8eab3a910:1">`print()`</span></span></span>

    -   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="016b94a069a8435c9b4f24bf357743e7"><span data-offset-key="016b94a069a8435c9b4f24bf357743e7:0">Are of type integer, floating-point or string</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="785e8d8328024e1ab475d0c54bdbd006"><span data-offset-key="785e8d8328024e1ab475d0c54bdbd006:0">Step 10: Introducing Variables</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="756b113fa0ec4206b9a600e85d9d900f"><span data-offset-key="756b113fa0ec4206b9a600e85d9d900f:0">We are slowly making progress toward our main goal, which is to print the </span><span data-offset-key="756b113fa0ec4206b9a600e85d9d900f:1">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="756b113fa0ec4206b9a600e85d9d900f:2"> multiplication table.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb"><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:0">In the first statement, we are printing </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:1">`5 * 1 = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:2">, and then changing the literals. To make it print </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:3">`5 * 2 = 10`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:4">, we are changing </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:5">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:6"> to </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:7">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:8">. Next, we are changing </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:9">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:10"> to </span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:11">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="b6ff298098f044aaaae4fcbc907ec9bb:12">. How do we make it a little simpler, so that our effort is reduced?</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,1,5*1))    5 * 1 = 5    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,2,5*2))    5 * 2 = 10    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,3,5*3))    5 * 3 = 15

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67f9d13634bb46ea9615ada974ff06a8"><span data-offset-key="67f9d13634bb46ea9615ada974ff06a8:0">Let’s try a different approach.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a"><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:0">What would happen if you replace </span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:1">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:2"> with </span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:3">`index`</span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:4">, and </span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:5">`5 * 1`</span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:6"> with </span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:7">`5 * index`</span><span data-offset-key="82909c14964c44838bdb1dd2308c006a:8">, and try to run it?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="776a3a8e52734e1687eacb8b8a49c68d"><span data-offset-key="776a3a8e52734e1687eacb8b8a49c68d:0">It gives an error! It says: “index is not defined”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5220db5918af4c089f78b50e2a16e234"><span data-offset-key="5220db5918af4c089f78b50e2a16e234:0">Let’s try and fix this, and execute </span><span data-offset-key="5220db5918af4c089f78b50e2a16e234:1">`index = 2`</span><span data-offset-key="5220db5918af4c089f78b50e2a16e234:2">. What would happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> index = 2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="48c81521858d48ffb72d4cc0c2e872c1"><span data-offset-key="48c81521858d48ffb72d4cc0c2e872c1:0">Aha! This compiles.</span></span></span>

        >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,index,5*index))    5 * 2 = 10

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="db22c6c0d8a04771b62901438b36d940"><span data-offset-key="db22c6c0d8a04771b62901438b36d940:0">And this statement is printing </span><span data-offset-key="db22c6c0d8a04771b62901438b36d940:1">`5 * 2 = 10`</span><span data-offset-key="db22c6c0d8a04771b62901438b36d940:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ee777fe7d41e4d328d3c3f8306926f19"><span data-offset-key="ee777fe7d41e4d328d3c3f8306926f19:0">Let’s try something else. Let’s make </span><span data-offset-key="ee777fe7d41e4d328d3c3f8306926f19:1">`index = 3`</span><span data-offset-key="ee777fe7d41e4d328d3c3f8306926f19:2">. What would happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> index = 3    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,index,5*index))    5 * 3 = 15

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dafdb9c10841422bb71d5949c2a290ae"><span data-offset-key="dafdb9c10841422bb71d5949c2a290ae:0">The same statement on being run, prints </span><span data-offset-key="dafdb9c10841422bb71d5949c2a290ae:1">`5 * 3 = 15`</span><span data-offset-key="dafdb9c10841422bb71d5949c2a290ae:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd"><span data-offset-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd:0">How can you check the value that </span><span data-offset-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd:1">`index`</span><span data-offset-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd:2"> has? Just type in </span><span data-offset-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd:3">`index`</span><span data-offset-key="c6d1fd452e1445b49d8b0ff19a1ae0cd:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> index    3    >>> print("{0} * {1} = {2}".format(5,index,5*index))    5 * 3 = 15

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937"><span data-offset-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937:1">`index`</span><span data-offset-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937:2"> symbol we have used here, is what is called a </span><span data-offset-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937:3">**variable**</span><span data-offset-key="4e5c7d2f25204efdb515d8a7d843c937:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d75b412300904a47ac03527541ca23a7"><span data-offset-key="d75b412300904a47ac03527541ca23a7:0">In Python, it’s also called a </span><span data-offset-key="d75b412300904a47ac03527541ca23a7:1">**name**</span><span data-offset-key="d75b412300904a47ac03527541ca23a7:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="08a9cf5aecec4df9b54c272df9fe76ac"><span data-offset-key="08a9cf5aecec4df9b54c272df9fe76ac:0">You can see that the value </span><span data-offset-key="08a9cf5aecec4df9b54c272df9fe76ac:1">`index`</span><span data-offset-key="08a9cf5aecec4df9b54c272df9fe76ac:2"> referring to, can change over the duration of a program.</span></span></span>
