<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="43f0a19964fe44b0b18039330edb1412"><span data-offset-key="43f0a19964fe44b0b18039330edb1412:0">Suppose we say a </span><span data-offset-key="43f0a19964fe44b0b18039330edb1412:1">`product =                                       product_of_two_numbers(1,2)`</span><span data-offset-key="43f0a19964fe44b0b18039330edb1412:2">, is this allowed?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5ada7717f1174dbe858aa9463fd9627c"><span data-offset-key="5ada7717f1174dbe858aa9463fd9627c:0">Let’s run this code, and see what’s stored in </span><span data-offset-key="5ada7717f1174dbe858aa9463fd9627c:1">`product`</span><span data-offset-key="5ada7717f1174dbe858aa9463fd9627c:2">.</span></span></span>

        >>> product = product_of_two_numbers(1,2)    2    >>> product

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f4aca201ea1e4a63805ff3d8748b9bdb"><span data-offset-key="f4aca201ea1e4a63805ff3d8748b9bdb:0">It’s empty.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="32b6c35ba9834d488cbc3aa602864e67"><span data-offset-key="32b6c35ba9834d488cbc3aa602864e67:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="32b6c35ba9834d488cbc3aa602864e67:1">`product_of_two_numbers()`</span><span data-offset-key="32b6c35ba9834d488cbc3aa602864e67:2"> method is not really returning anything back, to be used elsewhere.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3ff8c47b1fc64ff9b658407d91ca1f2f"><span data-offset-key="3ff8c47b1fc64ff9b658407d91ca1f2f:0">Have a look at some of the built-in Python functions, such as </span><span data-offset-key="3ff8c47b1fc64ff9b658407d91ca1f2f:1">`max()`</span><span data-offset-key="3ff8c47b1fc64ff9b658407d91ca1f2f:2"> for example.</span></span></span>

        >>> max(1,2,3)    3    >>> max(1,2,3,4)    4    >>> maximum = max(1,2,3,4)    >>> maximum    4    >>> maximum * 5    20

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436"><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:0">If I call </span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:1">`max()`</span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:2"> with four parameters, as in </span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:3">`maximum = max(1,2,3,4)`</span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:4">, the value </span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:5">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="68776a47456b494abfaf09324d5e9436:6"> gets stored in maximum.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e"><span data-offset-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e:0">Later on in the code that follows, we can say </span><span data-offset-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e:1">`maximum * 5`</span><span data-offset-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e:2">, or we can print the value of </span><span data-offset-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e:3">`maximum`</span><span data-offset-key="a3b04f0a212d46b180c6893f4a17e72e:4">, or a similar calculation. This gives our programs a lot more flexibility.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a7d9a977a27e4d94a1ff837de8d4357b"><span data-offset-key="a7d9a977a27e4d94a1ff837de8d4357b:0">So instead of just printing </span><span data-offset-key="a7d9a977a27e4d94a1ff837de8d4357b:1">`a*b`</span><span data-offset-key="a7d9a977a27e4d94a1ff837de8d4357b:2">, if this function could return a value, that would be quite useful.</span></span></span>

        >>> def product_of_two_numbers(a,b):    ...      product = a * b;    ...      return product    ...    >>> product_of_two_numbers(2,3)    6

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd"><span data-offset-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd:0">We are creating a variable </span><span data-offset-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd:1">`product`</span><span data-offset-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd:2"> and doing a </span><span data-offset-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd:3">`return product`</span><span data-offset-key="ee184bff5d324b4988ea3d52335b3afd:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9c9b9acad65e4f2fbe0412d5c865a1fb"><span data-offset-key="9c9b9acad65e4f2fbe0412d5c865a1fb:0">Lets run </span><span data-offset-key="9c9b9acad65e4f2fbe0412d5c865a1fb:1">`product_result =                                       product_of_two_numbers(2, 3)`</span></span></span>

        >>> product_result = product_of_two_numbers(2,3)    >>> product_result    6    >>> product_result * 10    60

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bd2b3dcd99584f36b591db499207a396"><span data-offset-key="bd2b3dcd99584f36b591db499207a396:0">You can see how simple it is to return values from a method!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5bb07ee9b72448c68c78c99ed07dff80"><span data-offset-key="5bb07ee9b72448c68c78c99ed07dff80:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c0c34721eb3e44b3b74754efb368beef"><span data-offset-key="c0c34721eb3e44b3b74754efb368beef:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fdd34cc1a7264eabb0772ed093cb6dfc"><span data-offset-key="fdd34cc1a7264eabb0772ed093cb6dfc:0">Learned how to return values from inside a method</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2ab5414803834e98a6ffca7325fc21f7"><span data-offset-key="2ab5414803834e98a6ffca7325fc21f7:0">Observed how we can store the values returned by a method call</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5553175045f44f58b7667001fbfe8f74"><span data-offset-key="5553175045f44f58b7667001fbfe8f74:0">Step 10: Programming Exercise PE-MD-02</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="828d969d74d14ca5931da1d552a7d564"><span data-offset-key="828d969d74d14ca5931da1d552a7d564:0">In this step let’s look at a couple of exercises about returning values from methods.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="22562872e3634546bfff9dc0fdf8f1ff"><span data-offset-key="22562872e3634546bfff9dc0fdf8f1ff:0">**Exercises**</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="312206f9dcca4a18a89a22e9146fbd83"><span data-offset-key="312206f9dcca4a18a89a22e9146fbd83:0">Write a method to return the sum of three integers.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e070c95499954007b62e17bcec63df81"><span data-offset-key="e070c95499954007b62e17bcec63df81:0">Write a method which takes as input two integers, representing two angles of a triangle, and computes the third angle.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b"><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:0">Hint: The sum of the angles in a triangle is </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:1">`180`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:2"> degrees. So if I am passing </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:3">`50`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:5">`50`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:6">, </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:7">`50`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:8"> plus </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:9">`50`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:10"> is </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:11">`100`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:12">. So some of three angles should be </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:13">`180`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:14">, so the third angle will be </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:15">`180 - 100`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:16">, which is </span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:17">`80`</span><span data-offset-key="cdee623670ab460fb9fc1fe3f20e9c6b:18">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="21c1a760af2741efa1d36847d8e86659"><span data-offset-key="21c1a760af2741efa1d36847d8e86659:0">**Solution 1**</span></span></span>

        >>>def sum_of_three_numbers(a, b, c):    ...     sum = a + b + c    ...     return sum    ...​    >>> sum_of_three_numbers(1,2,3)    6    >>> something = sum_of_three_numbers(1,2,3)    >>> something * 5    30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03"><span data-offset-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03:0">The shorter way of doing that would have been to have a temporary variable called instead of </span><span data-offset-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03:1">`sum`</span><span data-offset-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03:2">. We could directly </span><span data-offset-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03:3">`return a + b + c`</span><span data-offset-key="3ad7bac3cf1149058ef08e9ceb762b03:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> def sum_of_three_numbers(a, b, c):    ...     return a + b + c    ...    >>> something = sum_of_three_numbers(1,2,3)    >>> something * 5    30

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2"><span data-offset-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2:0">In methods, you can use </span><span data-offset-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2:1">`return expression`</span><span data-offset-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2:2"> as well. That </span><span data-offset-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2:3">`expression`</span><span data-offset-key="79e103a645684c139dd5447f115d82d2:4"> gets evaluated, and the value gets returned back. You’d see that the result remains the same.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c14ac2a5df804083a64c61e26e923788"><span data-offset-key="c14ac2a5df804083a64c61e26e923788:0">**Solution 2**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1949434077d7453c91ad70a35c966b6d"><span data-offset-key="1949434077d7453c91ad70a35c966b6d:0">The second is to write a method to take two integers, representing two angles of a triangle, and compute the third one.</span></span></span>

        >>> def calculate_third_angle(first, second) :    ...     return 180 - ( first + second )    ...    >>> calculate_third_angle(50, 20)    110

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c31b7f1286a74eceb23deb595639b472"><span data-offset-key="c31b7f1286a74eceb23deb595639b472:0">In your programming career, you would be writing a number of methods. It’s very important that you are comfortable doing so. Most of the methods that you write would return values back.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="19d8cbc720b047149f1bc1bcde2a300d"><span data-offset-key="19d8cbc720b047149f1bc1bcde2a300d:0">That’s the reason why we’re creating a lot of examples involving method calls.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8b493b0674064a08aaf4042896c20c35"><span data-offset-key="8b493b0674064a08aaf4042896c20c35:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bdde82435c3f4945a0c67cf99bdde22e"><span data-offset-key="bdde82435c3f4945a0c67cf99bdde22e:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="526697304bf34dc0b5a0bad28b7c822b"><span data-offset-key="526697304bf34dc0b5a0bad28b7c822b:0">Looked at a couple of exercises related to returning values from methods</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f2c7cf8949ff4652a956ee8efef490f1"><span data-offset-key="f2c7cf8949ff4652a956ee8efef490f1:0">Observed that returning expressions avoids creating unnecessary variables, and shortens method definitions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7ac875069df04c128c60578ee2da87cb"><span data-offset-key="7ac875069df04c128c60578ee2da87cb:0">Chapter 04 - Introduction To Python Platform</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="76922feeb5ae4ebf92dc7d7872f37753"><span data-offset-key="76922feeb5ae4ebf92dc7d7872f37753:0">Until now we had been using Python Shell to execute all our code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1a90e482e8164a1cb09170b29a463705"><span data-offset-key="1a90e482e8164a1cb09170b29a463705:0">In the real world, we’ll be write Python code in a variety of scripts. Before we would go into an IDE and use the IDE to write the script, we thought it would be useful for us to understand how you can write Python code without the benefit of an IDE.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8593c14922574a99b85f830c8701b2d4"><span data-offset-key="8593c14922574a99b85f830c8701b2d4:0">This would also help us understand the Python environment, in-depth.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="966d1eb304484afc99a082c0175fff2e"><span data-offset-key="966d1eb304484afc99a082c0175fff2e:0">In the next few steps, we’ll be looking at how to create simple Python scripts, using any text editor of your choice. Use Notepad, Notepad++. Editpad, or whichever text editing software you are comfortable with. We’ll see what involved in executing the program, and what’s happening in the background.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="45dd6aa2455c40979311f54aac1148ea"><span data-offset-key="45dd6aa2455c40979311f54aac1148ea:0">Here are a few videos you might want to look at.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="769f1fe916e2469c88bd1bc348dafb58"><span data-offset-key="769f1fe916e2469c88bd1bc348dafb58:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ORmDD1R7lNc" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8de7283c221e4002b21716e79bef0561"><span data-offset-key="8de7283c221e4002b21716e79bef0561:0">Writing and Executing your First Python Script</span></span></a><span data-key="37cbe1ebb13a495d896870f94b0fa2de"><span data-offset-key="37cbe1ebb13a495d896870f94b0fa2de:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b8e1bb88b241457b95a8e7479ca2c6b2"><span data-offset-key="b8e1bb88b241457b95a8e7479ca2c6b2:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HE-FC0csG68" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2e21614dffb4415e8dc4932dfd03bda2"><span data-offset-key="2e21614dffb4415e8dc4932dfd03bda2:0">Understanding Python Virtual Machine and bytecode</span></span></a><span data-key="ccd706ff48264e6a8e5ed99a48ae3473"><span data-offset-key="ccd706ff48264e6a8e5ed99a48ae3473:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4b8cf319ec0345d78dead6b4644856e9"><span data-offset-key="4b8cf319ec0345d78dead6b4644856e9:0">Step 01 - Writing and Executing Python Shell Programs</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cf2a15e8c8e241808a0e91adddd0fc95"><span data-offset-key="cf2a15e8c8e241808a0e91adddd0fc95:0">Here’s a recommended video to watch - </span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ORmDD1R7lNc" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c2633539e8e7431dacc186b18d6c99ce"><span data-offset-key="c2633539e8e7431dacc186b18d6c99ce:0">Writing and Executing your First Python Script</span></span></a><span data-key="5acad22b6c1d4b7c8edad3cfc03c8498"><span data-offset-key="5acad22b6c1d4b7c8edad3cfc03c8498:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6f377f0b43de47f18306b21e7fdb6833"><span data-offset-key="6f377f0b43de47f18306b21e7fdb6833:0">Let’s get started with creating a simple script file.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c5b9a8cb7bfb4295b7c97e23f5d76905"><span data-offset-key="c5b9a8cb7bfb4295b7c97e23f5d76905:0">We want to type in a simple Python script, or a piece of Python code, such as </span><span data-offset-key="c5b9a8cb7bfb4295b7c97e23f5d76905:1">`print("Hello world")`</span><span data-offset-key="c5b9a8cb7bfb4295b7c97e23f5d76905:2">. Does it get any simpler than this?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d36e3aa5904c4d3a9ce896c499b2b2ac"><span data-offset-key="d36e3aa5904c4d3a9ce896c499b2b2ac:0">We’ll save this into any folder on our hard disk, with a name ‘first.py’ .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a30338858cc54a7dba35638e22c83367"><span data-offset-key="a30338858cc54a7dba35638e22c83367:0">***first.py***</span></span></span>

    print("Hello world")

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d32d6d158c640ecbfec88b8ed4f9bd1"><span data-offset-key="1d32d6d158c640ecbfec88b8ed4f9bd1:0">The ‘.py’ is not really mandatory, but typically all python files end with a ‘.py’ extension.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="db5d834c809240c3b4001a4056040821"><span data-offset-key="db5d834c809240c3b4001a4056040821:0">Here’s how you can run it:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="80429cbeaa3748a4acd1027e1377a9d2"><span data-offset-key="80429cbeaa3748a4acd1027e1377a9d2:0">Launch your terminal, or command prompt</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="14cbf05005cf4f73a07228b915bbfa41"><span data-offset-key="14cbf05005cf4f73a07228b915bbfa41:0">‘cd’ to the folder where this python script file is saved</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6f307405b790471db1d64e3698680a3f"><span data-offset-key="6f307405b790471db1d64e3698680a3f:0">execute the command </span><span data-offset-key="6f307405b790471db1d64e3698680a3f:1">`python first.py`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="827930933b274bae9c520d527437c99d"><span data-offset-key="827930933b274bae9c520d527437c99d:0">You will see that </span><span data-offset-key="827930933b274bae9c520d527437c99d:1">`Hello World`</span><span data-offset-key="827930933b274bae9c520d527437c99d:2"> will be printed.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f6dc740878ba4a0f9664c0da3431a1e7"><span data-offset-key="f6dc740878ba4a0f9664c0da3431a1e7:0">If you are familiar with other programming languages, you would need a class, need to put the code in that class, and similar stuff.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="133ec62981cb4541a5cc36e0dc820c5b"><span data-offset-key="133ec62981cb4541a5cc36e0dc820c5b:0">While Python supports Object Oriented Programming, is not mandatory to create a class.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6e371aa24bc848e8b3c59ea9a527284c"><span data-offset-key="6e371aa24bc848e8b3c59ea9a527284c:0">It’s almost as if you’re typing commands, starting from the line one! That’s why we call it a python script.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f03f28c9640b4345bf79c0d3e35900f0"><span data-offset-key="f03f28c9640b4345bf79c0d3e35900f0:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8eb9f1f9dde245a38e9b15e13f794d69"><span data-offset-key="8eb9f1f9dde245a38e9b15e13f794d69:0">In this small step, we tried to create a simple python script, and we ran it from the command line. All we needed to do, was use the same command we use to launch up the python shell, and followed it up with a name of the file. We created a file called first.py, executed that, and were able to see the output on the console.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1e97cfb4d67d47ab8c0969610a1812ad"><span data-offset-key="1e97cfb4d67d47ab8c0969610a1812ad:0">As an exercise, try and add a few more methods and try to run those methods as well, as part of this script.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8036f8f46ee94a1f90257f2235971b60"><span data-offset-key="8036f8f46ee94a1f90257f2235971b60:0">Step 02 - Python virtual machine and bytecode</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="08eaa72be83a4a429ded7465d0bbaef3"><span data-offset-key="08eaa72be83a4a429ded7465d0bbaef3:0">In this step, let’s try and understand what’s happening in the background.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="76a33cfecb0043ecb9152241c5753439"><span data-offset-key="76a33cfecb0043ecb9152241c5753439:0">We wrote a simple piece of code using a text editor. We created a file named first.py, and all we did was: </span><span data-offset-key="76a33cfecb0043ecb9152241c5753439:1">`python3 first.py`</span><span data-offset-key="76a33cfecb0043ecb9152241c5753439:2">. If you look at other languages like Java for example, there is a separate compilation phase and then an execution phase. But with Python, just this command does both compilation and execution.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="65e74bb085fb4dc5a259e369829a75e7"><span data-offset-key="65e74bb085fb4dc5a259e369829a75e7:0">We saw that, as soon as we make a change and we run </span><span data-offset-key="65e74bb085fb4dc5a259e369829a75e7:1">`python3 first.py`</span><span data-offset-key="65e74bb085fb4dc5a259e369829a75e7:2"> , the change is compiled and executed as well!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0"><span data-offset-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0:0">In Python, there is an intermediate format called </span><span data-offset-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0:1">**Python byte code**</span><span data-offset-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0:2">. Code is first compiled to bytecode, and then executed on the </span><span data-offset-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0:3">**Python virtual machine**</span><span data-offset-key="ffbbba4a288c4f80a627bb1f33f1c7e0:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1e7a1cd6ca7f47d39535054cef5e582f"><span data-offset-key="1e7a1cd6ca7f47d39535054cef5e582f:0">When we installed Python, we installed both the python compiler and interpreter, as well as the virtual machine.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="566be2b1109943a8a171f6b4251e5c9c"><span data-offset-key="566be2b1109943a8a171f6b4251e5c9c:0">In Python, </span><span data-offset-key="566be2b1109943a8a171f6b4251e5c9c:1">`bytecode`</span><span data-offset-key="566be2b1109943a8a171f6b4251e5c9c:2"> is not standardized. Different implementations of Python have different byte code. There are about 80 Python implementations, like CPython and Jython.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9f41e5fd82a2445a94e526334919b167"><span data-offset-key="9f41e5fd82a2445a94e526334919b167:0">CPython is a Python implementation in C language.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e6528f3d4691435aafa9aa4da0c87343"><span data-offset-key="e6528f3d4691435aafa9aa4da0c87343:0">Jython is a Python implementation in Java language. The bytecode which Jython uses is actually Java bytecode, and you can run it on the Java virtual machine.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c4183c02e3de4f7bb86f1d5f3f4b586e"><span data-offset-key="c4183c02e3de4f7bb86f1d5f3f4b586e:0">Python leaves a lot of flexibility to the implementations of Python. They have the flexibility to choose the bytecode, and to choose the virtual machine that is compatible. The bytecode is tied to the specific virtual machine you are using. Therefore, if you’re using CPython to compile the bytecode, you’ll not be able to use Jython to run it.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9a009edc8dc74dcabda9d846ba33dd19"><span data-offset-key="9a009edc8dc74dcabda9d846ba33dd19:0">You should make sure, that whatever implementation you are using to compile, is the same one you’re using to run the code as well.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7c9d3227f6b745b087508c7e1c0c32f6"><span data-offset-key="7c9d3227f6b745b087508c7e1c0c32f6:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5268f722501a474ab2c829e767e71168"><span data-offset-key="5268f722501a474ab2c829e767e71168:0">A lot of this sounds like boring theory. Don’t worry about it. As a beginner, this might not be very important for you right now.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3536b85494d446ef806efb167f21c941"><span data-offset-key="3536b85494d446ef806efb167f21c941:0">It’s very important for you to understand the process. What’s happening is you were writing Python code, and when you ran the command </span><span data-offset-key="3536b85494d446ef806efb167f21c941:1">`python3 first.py`</span><span data-offset-key="3536b85494d446ef806efb167f21c941:2">, it is both compiled and executed. An intermediate format called bytecode is created, which is not really standardized in Python. The bytecode is executed in a Python virtual machine.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d9063503012e457a862716e59c8b267d"><span data-offset-key="d9063503012e457a862716e59c8b267d:0">The idea behind this quick section, is to give you a little bit of background on what’s happening behind the scenes. I’ll see you in the next section. Until then, bye-bye!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="85a78e49b5504c56a4f715e5d30bd049"><span data-offset-key="85a78e49b5504c56a4f715e5d30bd049:0">Chapter 05 - Introduction To VSCode</span></span></span>

It says </span><span data-offset-key="4a06ac6691ae4394bba92f9218c05f84:1">`'Hello World'`</span><span data-offset-key="4a06ac6691ae4394bba92f9218c05f84:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="64b2ec8f798b4b96b20e38ea7daad440"><span data-offset-key="64b2ec8f798b4b96b20e38ea7daad440:0">Step 03 - Execise - Write Multiplication Table Method with VSCode</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="421a536b4a0f448fabf2ac5c2491de24"><span data-offset-key="421a536b4a0f448fabf2ac5c2491de24:0">Let’s start with a simple exercise.
