<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2d70d9bac4f54e6883d3bd535c19e0ee"><span data-offset-key="2d70d9bac4f54e6883d3bd535c19e0ee:0">Here’s the video guide for this step:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="84ce567e268e4df5836724a543256437"><span data-offset-key="84ce567e268e4df5836724a543256437:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PvYSlWbXuCw" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b6b90c664d78482d8d7f90e9349a06d6"><span data-offset-key="b6b90c664d78482d8d7f90e9349a06d6:0">Write Your First Python Program with VSCode</span></span></a><span data-key="c8886a4dbc334ee194b670f3ccc2817d"><span data-offset-key="c8886a4dbc334ee194b670f3ccc2817d:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ca1c6e1c4a9c4b5ebb176b585245c772"><span data-offset-key="ca1c6e1c4a9c4b5ebb176b585245c772:0">Chapter 06 - Introducing Data Types and Conditionals</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8f92dd5edc2240808c545ffdb05c061e"><span data-offset-key="8f92dd5edc2240808c545ffdb05c061e:0">Welcome to this section, where we will talk about numeric data types, and conditional program execution. After looking at the numeric and boolean data types, we will turn our attention to executing code, based on logical conditions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ecccfb9f1ee04f34aae902d2f3209d18"><span data-offset-key="ecccfb9f1ee04f34aae902d2f3209d18:0">Step 01: Numeric Data Types</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965"><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:0">In previous sections, we created variables of this kind: </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:1">`number = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:2"> , </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:3">`value = 2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:4">, etc. The </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:5">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:6"> here is an integer, and integers represent numbers, such as </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:7">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:8">, </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:9">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:10">, </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:11">`6`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:12">, </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:13">`-1`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:14"> and </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:15">`-2`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:16">. In Python, the </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:17">`class`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:18"> for this particular data type is </span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:19">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="8b4061b2ec1e4519bb64d15867509965:20">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec"><span data-offset-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec:0">If you write code like </span><span data-offset-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec:1">`type(5)`</span><span data-offset-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec:2">, you’d get </span><span data-offset-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec:3">`'int'`</span><span data-offset-key="919e770fdb9a4f79a36101c13e8238ec:4"> as the output.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="42b31e01d2254f10b2792e34669799ca"><span data-offset-key="42b31e01d2254f10b2792e34669799ca:0">In Python, there are no primitive types. What does that mean? Every value that you see in a Python program, is an object, an instance of some </span><span data-offset-key="42b31e01d2254f10b2792e34669799ca:1">`class`</span><span data-offset-key="42b31e01d2254f10b2792e34669799ca:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae"><span data-offset-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae:0">In later sections, We’ll understand what is a </span><span data-offset-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae:1">`class`</span><span data-offset-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae:2">, and what is an object or an instance. For now, the most important thing for you to remember, is that behind every value, there is a </span><span data-offset-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae:3">`class`</span><span data-offset-key="25fb0a2fafb1497586871231b205e7ae:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8d39ec1a4c564c9bb71f825be5fb3772"><span data-offset-key="8d39ec1a4c564c9bb71f825be5fb3772:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c945b4241b8a47fab225461c478017fa"><span data-offset-key="c945b4241b8a47fab225461c478017fa:0">Let’s look at </span><span data-offset-key="c945b4241b8a47fab225461c478017fa:1">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="c945b4241b8a47fab225461c478017fa:2">, which is a floating point value.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8"><span data-offset-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8:0">If you go ahead and do </span><span data-offset-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8:1">`type(2.5)`</span><span data-offset-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8:2">, what would you see? You would see it’s of type \`</span><span data-offset-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="eee6d735209240dd92c023d7e1b504e8:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> type(2.5)    <class 'float'>    >>> type(2.55)    <class 'float'>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732"><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:0">When you perform a division operation between two integers, there is a chance that the result of the operation is a </span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:1">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:2">. If you do </span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:3">`5/2`</span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:4">, the result is </span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:5">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:6">. If we were to do </span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:7">`4/2`</span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:8">, even then it’s of type </span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:9">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="80e67a002654426aa8fe6df170d1c732:10">.</span></span></span>

        >>> type(5/2)    <class 'float'>    >>> type(4/2)    <class 'float'>    >>> 4/2    2.0    >>> 1 + 2    3

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7b725491700b42f39b1b63cdf0d33612"><span data-offset-key="7b725491700b42f39b1b63cdf0d33612:0">All the operations we looked at until now, can also be performed on floating point values.</span></span></span>

        >>> value1 = 4.5    >>> value2 = 3.2    >>> value1 + value2    7.7    >>> value1 - value2    1.2999999999999998    >>> value1 / value2    1.40625    >>> value1 % value2    1.2999999999999998

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="59d5c12e18384b858eeff4b3b1fd2839"><span data-offset-key="59d5c12e18384b858eeff4b3b1fd2839:0">`value1 - value2`</span><span data-offset-key="59d5c12e18384b858eeff4b3b1fd2839:1"> returns </span><span data-offset-key="59d5c12e18384b858eeff4b3b1fd2839:2">`1.299999999999998`</span><span data-offset-key="59d5c12e18384b858eeff4b3b1fd2839:3">. Why?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="256a559c940b4fe490d5919aab99c0ca"><span data-offset-key="256a559c940b4fe490d5919aab99c0ca:0">Floating point numbers don’t really represent accurate values. That’s one of the things you need to always keep in mind.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb"><span data-offset-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb:0">Typically, if you’re doing any highly sensitive financial calculations, don’t use </span><span data-offset-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb:1">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb:2">s to represent your values. Instead, use </span><span data-offset-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb:3">`Decimal`</span><span data-offset-key="ae8c983e64204238b164bfa5eac83edb:4">. More about it later.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344"><span data-offset-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344:0">Operations can also be performed between </span><span data-offset-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="b03819fc9f4147e281afc1c0d43ea344:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i + value1    14.5    >>> i - value1    5.5    >>> i / value1    2.2222222222222223    >>>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019"><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:0">Result of an operation between a </span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:2"> and a </span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:4">, is always a </span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:5">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="29ba14575ccd44e7aab1736715f06019:6">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e7f62b0a295841c99d3e5f420e5d48dc"><span data-offset-key="e7f62b0a295841c99d3e5f420e5d48dc:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="421e6ea251c1498793e94c316bd88e68"><span data-offset-key="421e6ea251c1498793e94c316bd88e68:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292"><span data-offset-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292:0">Looked at the two basic numeric types: </span><span data-offset-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="f2de26b61d424a18ab44931d4efa5292:4">.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d"><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:0">Saw the basic operations you can do among </span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:2">s, among </span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:4">s, and also between </span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:5">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:6">s and </span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:7">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="2cff48db5b154ecfa3f7a8ab69dca54d:8">s.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="055c91623d6d4402870f3200a4343242"><span data-offset-key="055c91623d6d4402870f3200a4343242:0">Step 02: Programming Exercise PE-DT-01</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0efc51bc07424bc380c5419a38397fab"><span data-offset-key="0efc51bc07424bc380c5419a38397fab:0">In this step, let’s do a simple exercise with numeric values.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8bd6ec99be1440f48b8b9c4b8b1d1ae1"><span data-offset-key="8bd6ec99be1440f48b8b9c4b8b1d1ae1:0">**Exercises**</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635"><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:0">You need to create a method called </span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:1">`simple_interest`</span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:2">, and pass three parameters: </span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:3">`principal`</span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:5">`interest`</span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:7">`duration`</span><span data-offset-key="90c46789970f4080b52633212c009635:8"> (in years). You also want to calculate the amount after the specific duration, and return it back. Call this method with a few example values.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1"><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:0">For example, if you want to call </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:1">`simple_interest`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:2"> with </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:3">`10000`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:4">, with an interest of </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:5">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:6"> percent, for a duration of </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:7">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:8"> years, the correct answer would be as follows: </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:9">`10000`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:10"> is the principal. In addition to </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:11">`10000`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:12">, you get the interest. The interest for one year is </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:13">`10000 * 0.05`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:14">, as the interest figure is in percentage.So that’s </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:15">`500`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:16"> a year, into </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:17">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:18"> which is </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:19">`2500`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:20">. The result would be </span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:21">`12500`</span><span data-offset-key="fffc0838cecf486e99a519bd776da0e1:22">, and this value should be printed.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8eea52897c204770a6cb56dc39f612b5"><span data-offset-key="8eea52897c204770a6cb56dc39f612b5:0">**Solution 1**</span></span></span>

        def calculate_simple_interest(principal, interest, duration) :            return principal * (1 + interest * 0.01 * duration)​    print(calculate_simple_interest(10000,5,5))

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ada552a73c9548a28a32d8ffeb29d53d"><span data-offset-key="ada552a73c9548a28a32d8ffeb29d53d:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9f55fede571542c8b3dfb83bb65257c7"><span data-offset-key="9f55fede571542c8b3dfb83bb65257c7:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a06b8f6e1908475f9372f29bb3250a2d"><span data-offset-key="a06b8f6e1908475f9372f29bb3250a2d:0">Wrote a very simple method to do a simple interest calculation</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="486640f55f004cef9655afe1a61cd4ba"><span data-offset-key="486640f55f004cef9655afe1a61cd4ba:0">Step 03: Puzzles On Numeric Types</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a96aabc150234c0b94c876cb5b3f0e59"><span data-offset-key="a96aabc150234c0b94c876cb5b3f0e59:0">In this section, we are looking at numeric types. In this specific step, we would be looking at a few puzzles related to values of these types.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6503eb2516444661a5dc6b88256c0486"><span data-offset-key="6503eb2516444661a5dc6b88256c0486:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f"><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:0">Let’s create a simple variable </span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:1">`i = 1`</span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:2">. </span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:3">`i = i + 1`</span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:4">. What would be the value of </span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:5">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="d0647aeba0884181be8ecd9e8a5fd06f:6"> after that?</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 1    >>> i = i + 1    >>> i    2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c"><span data-offset-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c:0">It would be </span><span data-offset-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c:1">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c:2">. There is a shortcut way of doing the same thing, by using the </span><span data-offset-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c:3">`+=`</span><span data-offset-key="c491ba29eee24f8e98f9a9269ee05a6c:4"> operator.</span></span></span>

        >>> i += 1    >>> i    3

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25"><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:0">Typically in other programming languages, you can do something of this kind: </span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:1">`i++`</span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:2">. There is no provision in Python to use increment operators like </span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:3">`++`</span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:4">, in either prefix or suffix mode, like </span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:5">`++i`</span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:6">, or </span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:7">`i++`</span><span data-offset-key="62b41069845249999928f14899abbb25:8">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i++      File "<stdin>", line 1        i++          ^    SyntaxError: invalid syntax    >>> ++i    3

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="38786f6dfbe14ae19f71c028263bbc7c"><span data-offset-key="38786f6dfbe14ae19f71c028263bbc7c:0">Let’s look at compound assignments.</span></span></span>

        >>> i += 1    >>> i    4    >>> i -= 1    >>> i    3    >>> i /= 1    >>> i *= 2    >>> i    6.0

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9328cdb597e545d5ac266dbadea354ff"><span data-offset-key="9328cdb597e545d5ac266dbadea354ff:0">What you see here, is Dynamic Typing in Python. The type of a variable can change during the lifetime of the program.</span></span></span>

    >>> i = 2>>> type(i)<type 'int'>>>> i = i/2.0>>> type(i)<type 'float'>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b"><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:0">Let’s create a couple more numbers. </span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:1">`number1 = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:3">`number2 = 2`</span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:4">. What could be the result of </span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:5">`number1 / number2`</span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:6">? You know it, it’s </span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:7">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="915898287fec4c4b95baa8208341df5b:8"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1"><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:0">`number1 // nummber2`</span><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:1"> truncates the value of </span><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:2">`2.5`</span><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:3">, to </span><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:4">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="c9b4f7bd80ba4a6ebfc62508e4d1fdb1:5">.</span></span></span>

        >>> number1//number2    2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629"><span data-offset-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629:0">If you can do </span><span data-offset-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629:1">`number1 // number2`</span><span data-offset-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629:2">, can you also do this: </span><span data-offset-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629:3">`number1 //= number2`</span><span data-offset-key="ed69069c6ca042f292c6de37fe352629:4">?</span></span></span>

        >>> number1 //= 2    >>> number1    2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3"><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:0">`5 ** 3`</span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:1"> is </span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:2">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:3"> ‘to the power of’ </span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:4">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:5">, which is </span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:6">`5 * 5 * 5`</span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:7">, or </span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:8">`125`</span><span data-offset-key="204605ddffc54217aa09ecbc1a633ee3:9">.</span></span></span>

        >>> 5 ** 3    125    >>> pow(5,3)    125

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2a5f4cdf645347e9befaebd5a9f923dc"><span data-offset-key="2a5f4cdf645347e9befaebd5a9f923dc:0">This can also be achieved by invoking </span><span data-offset-key="2a5f4cdf645347e9befaebd5a9f923dc:1">`pow(5, 3)`</span><span data-offset-key="2a5f4cdf645347e9befaebd5a9f923dc:2">. We have an operator, as well as a method at our disposal.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a2845dc354284213bf61599e2859cbce"><span data-offset-key="a2845dc354284213bf61599e2859cbce:0">The last thing we will look at, are type conversion functions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf"><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:0">If you need to convert an </span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:2"> value to a </span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:4">, or a </span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:5">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:6"> to an </span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:7">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="d23cf31592cf4330880feec0c8202abf:8">.</span></span></span>

        >>> int(5.6)    5

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a"><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:0">What if you want to round a value? </span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:1">`5.6`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:2"> is nearer to </span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:3">`6`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:4"> than </span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:5">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:6">. You can use a function called </span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:7">`round()`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:8">, and here,</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:9">`round(5.6)`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:10"> gives the correct result </span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:11">`6`</span><span data-offset-key="fee9d2e4070d44db88c80baf460b963a:12">.</span></span></span>

        >>> round(5.6)    6    >>> round(5.4)    5    >>> round(5.5)    6

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8ea96771f09648baa4d6e81829df54a8"><span data-offset-key="8ea96771f09648baa4d6e81829df54a8:0">`round()`</span><span data-offset-key="8ea96771f09648baa4d6e81829df54a8:1"> can also allows you to specify number of decimals in the result.</span></span></span>

        >>> round(5.67, 1)    5.7    >>> round(5.678, 2)    5.68

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69"><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:0">You can also convert </span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:1">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:2"> to </span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:3">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:4">, by using the function </span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:5">`float()`</span><span data-offset-key="fd9d16c49ff44ba28b3023ae0c2c7e69:6">.</span></span></span>

        >>> float(5)    5.0

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6167b4ff0f544d23acecd82ec8996dd5"><span data-offset-key="6167b4ff0f544d23acecd82ec8996dd5:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3a2239a6d8b94ac9b73eeda2353ccde6"><span data-offset-key="3a2239a6d8b94ac9b73eeda2353ccde6:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cb7ebea5108049908c578de36c14980d"><span data-offset-key="cb7ebea5108049908c578de36c14980d:0">Looked at a few corner cases related to your numeric types.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3a9009193d6c4a8ca6e1b7819e3e2b08"><span data-offset-key="3a9009193d6c4a8ca6e1b7819e3e2b08:0">Examined the different operators available for use with values of numeric types</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fb921d3319db4278b1b8ee9786f84a1a"><span data-offset-key="fb921d3319db4278b1b8ee9786f84a1a:0">Learned about the usage of type conversion functions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aa3f422003f8495c9562a2f3e2e7700f"><span data-offset-key="aa3f422003f8495c9562a2f3e2e7700f:0">Step 04: Introducing Boolean Type</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6c2997d0ca1d4d9e9824e94e03be28bb"><span data-offset-key="6c2997d0ca1d4d9e9824e94e03be28bb:0">We will now shift our attention to the </span><span data-offset-key="6c2997d0ca1d4d9e9824e94e03be28bb:1">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="6c2997d0ca1d4d9e9824e94e03be28bb:2"> data type.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8e982091f94c43d6b2c723b2521ade8b"><span data-offset-key="8e982091f94c43d6b2c723b2521ade8b:0">A boolean value is something which can be either “true” or “false”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="18e90596d15144a59cd1af5cf35588e3"><span data-offset-key="18e90596d15144a59cd1af5cf35588e3:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f"><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:0">In Python, “true” is represented by </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:1">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:2">, and “false” by </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:3">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:4">. It’s important to remember that it’s </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:5">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:6"> with a capital </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:7">`'T'`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:8">, and </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:9">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:10"> with a capital </span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:11">`'F'`</span><span data-offset-key="f326f2a1fa4849c3a98ecf043729dd3f:12">.</span></span></span>

        >>> True    True    >>> False    False    >>> true    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    NameError: name 'true' is not defined    >>> false    Traceback (most recent call last):      File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>    NameError: name 'false' is not defined

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="906192392e56400693cb6cdc775e9112"><span data-offset-key="906192392e56400693cb6cdc775e9112:0">The boolean variable </span><span data-offset-key="906192392e56400693cb6cdc775e9112:1">`is_even`</span><span data-offset-key="906192392e56400693cb6cdc775e9112:2"> indicates whether a number is even or not.</span></span></span>

        >>> is_even = True    >>> is_odd = False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0"><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:0">Let’s create a variable </span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:1">`i = 10`</span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:2">. We want to find out if </span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:3">`i > 15`</span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:4">. What do you think is the result? </span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:5">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="b5d2fcf27b0b4845b3af16b0fe1795a0:6">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 10    >>> i > 15    False    >>> i < 15    True

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b9dfe616882b44f092a46533fb9eeafb"><span data-offset-key="b9dfe616882b44f092a46533fb9eeafb:0">In general, boolean values can represent the result of logical conditions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69"><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:0">Let’s look at other operations that can result in </span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:1">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:2"> values. We looked at </span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:3">`>`</span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:5">`<`</span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:6">. Another operation which you can perform, is </span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:7">`>=`</span><span data-offset-key="3c74f06f1a2d45d8a7b82d29494daf69:8">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i >= 15    False    >>> i >= 10    True    >>> i > 10    False    >>> i <= 10    True    >>> i < 10    False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519"><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:0">`==`</span><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:1"> is the comparison operator. We are only comparing the value of </span><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:2">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:3"> against </span><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:4">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="2f580847e5ac458aba5a3f15109c2519:5">, not changing its value.</span></span></span>

        >>> i == 10    True    >>> i == 11    False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2077916d609a4491a5dfd37b12480975"><span data-offset-key="2077916d609a4491a5dfd37b12480975:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c6a2e80659e1458393e0bfbf78f4219f"><span data-offset-key="c6a2e80659e1458393e0bfbf78f4219f:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="85213f90f5404ce387191d2abcad53d1"><span data-offset-key="85213f90f5404ce387191d2abcad53d1:0">Were introduced to the </span><span data-offset-key="85213f90f5404ce387191d2abcad53d1:1">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="85213f90f5404ce387191d2abcad53d1:2"> data type</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c02c0c55d46846128c6e49a821aa6e0d"><span data-offset-key="c02c0c55d46846128c6e49a821aa6e0d:0">Learned that </span><span data-offset-key="c02c0c55d46846128c6e49a821aa6e0d:1">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="c02c0c55d46846128c6e49a821aa6e0d:2"> variables are useful handy while testing logical conditions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8fbd0901cb60469395eb416739b7b809"><span data-offset-key="8fbd0901cb60469395eb416739b7b809:0">Step 05: Introducing Conditionals</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="81acb637022446aeb7c40fde50669865"><span data-offset-key="81acb637022446aeb7c40fde50669865:0">In this step, let’s look at </span><span data-offset-key="81acb637022446aeb7c40fde50669865:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="81acb637022446aeb7c40fde50669865:2"> statement.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="60f6eb461d584528809da275db02bb90"><span data-offset-key="60f6eb461d584528809da275db02bb90:0">Sometimes you need to execute code only when certain conditions are true. You can use a </span><span data-offset-key="60f6eb461d584528809da275db02bb90:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="60f6eb461d584528809da275db02bb90:2"> condition, which is the simplest conditional in Python. Let’s look at an example.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="251f2282e8f545c79ef1593a87e97c71"><span data-offset-key="251f2282e8f545c79ef1593a87e97c71:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938"><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:0">Let’s say </span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:2"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:3">`5`</span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:4">. You want to print something, only if </span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:5">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:6"> has a value greater than </span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:7">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="6ed04e0e22834c6d9f7f8a77a20bf938:8">. How do you do that?</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 5    >>> if i>3:    ...     print(f"{i} is greater than 3")    ...    5 is greater than 3

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3"><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:0">The syntax of the </span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:2"> is very simple: </span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:3">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:4"> followed by a condition; with the condition you want to check. It looks like: </span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:5">`if i>3: ...`</span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:6"> You need to indent the body of the </span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:7">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:8"> with </span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:9">`<SPACE>`</span><span data-offset-key="7abcb02efbef4f4eb269eb248bda2fb3:10">s as usual.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88"><span data-offset-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88:0">Let’s say </span><span data-offset-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88:2"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88:3">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="7e02069a41144c05abd88bd0fffe9c88:4">. What would happen if we execute the same code again?</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 2    >>> if i>3:    ...     print(f"{i} is greater than 3")    ...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2"><span data-offset-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2:0">You would see that nothing is printed to the console. Based on the value of </span><span data-offset-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2:2"> , either the statement is executed, or it’s not. That’s what an </span><span data-offset-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2:3">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="ec6d6c5ffa034a94af6135e0280266f2:4"> helps us to do.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad"><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:0">The way you can think about an </span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:2">, is the body of code under the </span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:3">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:4"> is executed only when this condition is </span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:5">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:6">. If this condition is not </span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:7">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="1d00ae25f9034e4eaa5503f850e948ad:8">, that code is not executed at all.</span></span></span>

        >>> if(False):    ...   print("False")    ...    >>> if(True):    ...   print("True")    ...    True

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432"><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:0">Let’s take two different numbers, say </span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:1">`a = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:2">, and </span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:3">`b = 7`</span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:4">. We want to compare them, and predict if </span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:5">`a`</span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:6"> is greater that </span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:7">`b`</span><span data-offset-key="4962565a8d8a4971aa7909ec3d6de432:8"> .</span></span></span>

        >>> a = 5    >>> b = 7    >>> if(a>b):    ...   print("a is greater than b")    ...​    >>> a = 9    >>> if(a>b):    ...   print("a is greater than b")    ...    a is greater than b

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="391a39c5728a432297ba6fba7c4ec4d8"><span data-offset-key="391a39c5728a432297ba6fba7c4ec4d8:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="19dd541f73de4792893862ea482daf19"><span data-offset-key="19dd541f73de4792893862ea482daf19:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="85ee1c8df8a6451eadd7f7d6c14eec5d"><span data-offset-key="85ee1c8df8a6451eadd7f7d6c14eec5d:0">Were introduced to the </span><span data-offset-key="85ee1c8df8a6451eadd7f7d6c14eec5d:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="85ee1c8df8a6451eadd7f7d6c14eec5d:2"> statement, the simplest Python conditional</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="04a3a64c3a974d0da20f553d949038b5"><span data-offset-key="04a3a64c3a974d0da20f553d949038b5:0">Understood how an </span><span data-offset-key="04a3a64c3a974d0da20f553d949038b5:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="04a3a64c3a974d0da20f553d949038b5:2"> helps in implementing conditional program logic</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e62d683b9dce4e98811aa4571047ac3b"><span data-offset-key="e62d683b9dce4e98811aa4571047ac3b:0">Step 06: Classroom Exercise CE-DT-01</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2e39bbc824aa4523aaec3e7d4268e27c"><span data-offset-key="2e39bbc824aa4523aaec3e7d4268e27c:0">In this step, let’s look at a couple of exercises with the if statement.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="05941683b51441b3bbcede8b201696e5"><span data-offset-key="05941683b51441b3bbcede8b201696e5:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b"><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:0">Let’s say we define four variables: </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:1">`a = 1`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:3">`b = 2`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:4"> , </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:5">`c = 3`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:7">`d = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:8">. we want to find out, if </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:9">`a + b`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:10"> is greater than </span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:11">`c + d`</span><span data-offset-key="bd581be815c442e897735c938d8aa80b:12">.</span></span></span>

        >>> a = 1    >>> b = 2    >>> c = 3    >>> d = 5    >>> if a+b > c+d :    ...    print("a+b > c +d")    ...    >>> a = 9    >>> if a+b > c+d :    ...    print("a+b > c +d")    ...    a+b > c +d

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425"><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:0">Let’s say we are given three values meant to be the angles of a triangle. Their values are </span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:1">`angle1 = 30`</span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:3">`angle2 = 20`</span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:5">`angle3 = 60`</span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:6">. You want to find out if these three angles actually form a valid triangle. You know that the sum of the angles of a triangle is always </span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:7">`180`</span><span data-offset-key="201eb007e5754161b12437d37ec78425:8"> degrees.</span></span></span>

        >>> angle1 = 30    >>> angle2 = 20    >>> angle3 = 60    >>> if(angle1 + angle2 + angle3 == 180):    ...      print("Valid Triangle")    ...    >>> angle2 = 90    >>> if(angle1 + angle2 + angle3 == 180):    ...      print("Valid Triangle")    ...    Valid Triangle

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="937f0a4b89f641c5b2edaa63023689b2"><span data-offset-key="937f0a4b89f641c5b2edaa63023689b2:0">The last exercise is to check if a number is even or not.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2e210e1a380c4510860d017bce892955"><span data-offset-key="2e210e1a380c4510860d017bce892955:0">Hint L you need to use one of the operators we talked about earlier. That’s right, use the modulo operator </span><span data-offset-key="2e210e1a380c4510860d017bce892955:1">`%`</span><span data-offset-key="2e210e1a380c4510860d017bce892955:2">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 2    >>> if(i%2==0):    ...   print("i is even")    ...    i is even​    >>> i = 3    >>> if(i%2==0):    ...   print("i is even")    ...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="00c139be3105416a8c8cc44878c2a3e8"><span data-offset-key="00c139be3105416a8c8cc44878c2a3e8:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5c458f8ed14848199f323e29459daceb"><span data-offset-key="5c458f8ed14848199f323e29459daceb:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0af84cb13a8f4a189faf071c21226eb9"><span data-offset-key="0af84cb13a8f4a189faf071c21226eb9:0">Looked at a few exercises related to the if statement, for writing and testing conditions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b73adee0135244ddb35c118ba8c17670"><span data-offset-key="b73adee0135244ddb35c118ba8c17670:0">Step 07 - Logical Operators - and or not</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be"><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:0">In this step, let’s look at the different operators that can be used on </span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:1">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:2"> values. These operators are called logical operators - </span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:3">`and`</span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:5">`or`</span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:6"> , </span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:7">`not`</span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:8"> and </span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:9">`^`</span><span data-offset-key="51cfde1acf154bd98e9ce0d3539b02be:10"> (xor).</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003"><span data-offset-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003:0">Let’s say we have a value </span><span data-offset-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003:1">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003:2">, and the other </span><span data-offset-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003:3">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="ca7c94dc60754887819d8f978e411003:4">, and we want to play around with them.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5"><span data-offset-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5:0">Logical operator </span><span data-offset-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5:1">`and`</span><span data-offset-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5:2"> returns true only when both operands are </span><span data-offset-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="61774a83a7b04112b0d1efbf9e96d2a5:4">.</span></span></span>

        >>> True and False    False    >>> True and True    True    >>> True and False    False    >>> False and True    False    >>> False and False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57"><span data-offset-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57:0">Logical operator </span><span data-offset-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57:1">`or`</span><span data-offset-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57:2"> returns true when atleast one of the operands is </span><span data-offset-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="e9f5c9091c2f4ac8af2fc86136d10c57:4">.</span></span></span>

        False    >>> True or False    True    >>> False or True    True    >>> True or True    True    >>> False or False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="08c5e6c34e204532a09f9bd245f21cc3"><span data-offset-key="08c5e6c34e204532a09f9bd245f21cc3:0">Logical operator </span><span data-offset-key="08c5e6c34e204532a09f9bd245f21cc3:1">`not`</span><span data-offset-key="08c5e6c34e204532a09f9bd245f21cc3:2"> returns negation.</span></span></span>

        False    >>> not True    False    >>> not(True)    False    >>> not False    True    >>> not(False)    True

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72"><span data-offset-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72:0">The XOR operation, denoted by the </span><span data-offset-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72:1">`^`</span><span data-offset-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72:2"> operator, is </span><span data-offset-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="604360128d514486975e71b23ee89c72:4"> when operands have different boolean values.</span></span></span>

        >>> True ^ True    False    >>> True ^ False    True    >>> False ^ True    True    >>> False ^ False    False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f39e47b562ca479fb5112a8cfdf2af3e"><span data-offset-key="f39e47b562ca479fb5112a8cfdf2af3e:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="63c696aee7fb40a78a50c0d5065baabd"><span data-offset-key="63c696aee7fb40a78a50c0d5065baabd:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40"><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:0">Looked at the logical operators that act on boolean values, such as </span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:1">`and`</span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:3">`or`</span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:5">`not`</span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="46870958cc834658b816a6548e4f1f40:7">`^`</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214"><span data-offset-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214:0">Explored each of these operators, finding out when they return </span><span data-offset-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214:1">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214:2">, and when </span><span data-offset-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214:3">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="ac3af49d9be14e7abbbbb08eb45a1214:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a5da05035ed94422aa45bfa2020757af"><span data-offset-key="a5da05035ed94422aa45bfa2020757af:0">Step 08: Puzzles On Logical Operators</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="68bd99837961402a931d0bb1945c36c3"><span data-offset-key="68bd99837961402a931d0bb1945c36c3:0">In this step, Let’s look at a few simple puzzles to look at the logical operators.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="04ec2ee53bed41888de7c04ef1b08e7a"><span data-offset-key="04ec2ee53bed41888de7c04ef1b08e7a:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c"><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:0">Let’s say </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:2"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:3">`10`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:4">, and </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:5">`j`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:6"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:7">`15`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:8">. You want to find out if both </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:9">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:10"> and </span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:11">`j`</span><span data-offset-key="aa87d929d71f49b0aa2db29f86c0949c:12"> are even. How do you do that?</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 10    >>> j = 15    >>> if i%2==0 and j%2==0:    ...   print("i and j are even")    ...    >>> j = 14    >>> if i%2==0 and j%2==0:    ...   print("i and j are even")    ...    i and j are even​    >>> if i%2==0 or j%2==0:    ...      File "<stdin>", line 2        ^    IndentationError: expected an indented block    >>> if i%2==0 or j%2==0:    ...   print("atleast one of i and j are even")    ...    atleast one of i and j are even

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1"><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:0">If we want to find out if at least one of </span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:3">`j`</span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:4"> is even, we can use the </span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:5">`or`</span><span data-offset-key="20e59f86c0d14e608f400a7a6bb1f1e1:6"> operator.</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 15    >>> j    14    >>> if i%2==0 or j%2==0:    ...   print("atleast one of i and j are even")    ...    atleast one of i and j are even    >>> j = 23    >>> if i%2==0 or j%2==0:    ...   print("atleast one of i and j are even")    ...    >>> i    15

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="75123cbe8ef548aca1f2626e80c5f049"><span data-offset-key="75123cbe8ef548aca1f2626e80c5f049:0">Now try and guess the value of this. </span><span data-offset-key="75123cbe8ef548aca1f2626e80c5f049:1">`if(True ^ False):                                       print("Message")`</span></span></span>

        >>> if(True ^ False):    ...     print("This will Print")    ...    This will Print    >>> if(False ^ True):    ...     print("This will Print")    ...    This will Print    >>> if(True ^ True):    ...     print("This will Print")    ...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="44461251aba54c99b01d9bcdcd02a5ef"><span data-offset-key="44461251aba54c99b01d9bcdcd02a5ef:0">Xor operation using </span><span data-offset-key="44461251aba54c99b01d9bcdcd02a5ef:1">`^`</span><span data-offset-key="44461251aba54c99b01d9bcdcd02a5ef:2"> - message will get printed if the operands are different.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="342e8d091bf34a7291a5804bfaa68fab"><span data-offset-key="342e8d091bf34a7291a5804bfaa68fab:0">What would happen if both of them are </span><span data-offset-key="342e8d091bf34a7291a5804bfaa68fab:1">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="342e8d091bf34a7291a5804bfaa68fab:2">? No message is printed.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948"><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:0">So you would use </span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:1">`^`</span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:2"> in situations, where you’d want one of the operands to be </span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:4">, and the other to be </span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:5">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="2d7567dd175746d08739b9f156226948:6">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05"><span data-offset-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05:0">Let’s say, </span><span data-offset-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05:1">`x = 5`</span><span data-offset-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05:2">, and you want to check </span><span data-offset-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05:3">`if not x == 6:                                       print("This")`</span><span data-offset-key="0ba47694b25641109d64713c52a06a05:4">. What will be the result of running this code?</span></span></span>

        >>> x = 5    >>> if not x == 6:    ...   print("This")    ...    This    >>> x = 6    >>> if not x == 6:    ...   print("This")    ...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fa54895305da4214a4fdf4203225670d"><span data-offset-key="fa54895305da4214a4fdf4203225670d:0">Actually, there is a shortcut for such a condition: </span><span data-offset-key="fa54895305da4214a4fdf4203225670d:1">`if x != 6 : print("This")`</span><span data-offset-key="fa54895305da4214a4fdf4203225670d:2">.</span></span></span>

        >>> if x!=6:    ...   print("This")    ...    >>> x=5    >>> if x!=6:    ...   print("This")    ...    This

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc"><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:0">`int()`</span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:1"> is a conversion function, which when given say a </span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:2">`float`</span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:3"> value, returns an </span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:4">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:5"> value. Consider </span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:6">`int(True)`</span><span data-offset-key="c3d961f1813049f5983c26ea803163bc:7">, what would happen?</span></span></span>

        >>> int(True)    1    >>> int(False)    0

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="de476d77c414408bac29db4a40d55c0b"><span data-offset-key="de476d77c414408bac29db4a40d55c0b:0">`int(True)`</span><span data-offset-key="de476d77c414408bac29db4a40d55c0b:1"> returns 1. </span><span data-offset-key="de476d77c414408bac29db4a40d55c0b:2">`int(False)`</span><span data-offset-key="de476d77c414408bac29db4a40d55c0b:3"> returns 0.</span></span></span>

        >>> x = -6    >>> if x:    ...   print("something")    ...    something

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f9069e556f8d43fd91bc936e15be757f"><span data-offset-key="f9069e556f8d43fd91bc936e15be757f:0">One of the most interesting facts about boolean stuff, is anything which is non-zero, is considered to be </span><span data-offset-key="f9069e556f8d43fd91bc936e15be757f:1">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="f9069e556f8d43fd91bc936e15be757f:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2fea1dd695ea474fa0501184abd58450"><span data-offset-key="2fea1dd695ea474fa0501184abd58450:0">`0`</span><span data-offset-key="2fea1dd695ea474fa0501184abd58450:1"> is the only integer value which is considered to be </span><span data-offset-key="2fea1dd695ea474fa0501184abd58450:2">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="2fea1dd695ea474fa0501184abd58450:3">.</span></span></span>

        >>> bool(6)    True    >>> bool(-6)    True    >>> bool(0)    False    >>>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6"><span data-offset-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6:0">So, if I have a value of </span><span data-offset-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6:1">`x = -6`</span><span data-offset-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6:2">, and execute </span><span data-offset-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6:3">`if x: print("something")`</span><span data-offset-key="e4ee2f59a9144b92860d7898583c08e6:4"> what do you think will happen?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f05d8f8637eb44caa65995cfa4f9de50"><span data-offset-key="f05d8f8637eb44caa65995cfa4f9de50:0">`"something"`</span><span data-offset-key="f05d8f8637eb44caa65995cfa4f9de50:1"> will be printed.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268"><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:0">You can use the function </span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:1">`bool()`</span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:2">, to convert </span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:3">`int`</span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:4"> to a </span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:5">`bool`</span><span data-offset-key="9cccae88d15d48ff801a311c98133268:6"> value.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="44267001b302474ba0de21ff891729bc"><span data-offset-key="44267001b302474ba0de21ff891729bc:0">`bool(6)`</span><span data-offset-key="44267001b302474ba0de21ff891729bc:1"> returns </span><span data-offset-key="44267001b302474ba0de21ff891729bc:2">`True`</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="956a5ae22eaf4fe2a65c39a4a9b0e20b"><span data-offset-key="956a5ae22eaf4fe2a65c39a4a9b0e20b:0">`bool(-6)`</span><span data-offset-key="956a5ae22eaf4fe2a65c39a4a9b0e20b:1"> returns </span><span data-offset-key="956a5ae22eaf4fe2a65c39a4a9b0e20b:2">`True`</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1ca8e950125c4a2d924946de6fe756bf"><span data-offset-key="1ca8e950125c4a2d924946de6fe756bf:0">`bool(0)`</span><span data-offset-key="1ca8e950125c4a2d924946de6fe756bf:1"> returns </span><span data-offset-key="1ca8e950125c4a2d924946de6fe756bf:2">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="1ca8e950125c4a2d924946de6fe756bf:3">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9"><span data-offset-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9:0">Except for </span><span data-offset-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9:1">`bool(0)`</span><span data-offset-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9:2">, all the other results would be </span><span data-offset-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="aba2de50c6404d249d4a09a09c77eff9:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1982661a45f040238618beefc89d77f5"><span data-offset-key="1982661a45f040238618beefc89d77f5:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f69af5f930ef4df9b4b0e66b402aeb6c"><span data-offset-key="f69af5f930ef4df9b4b0e66b402aeb6c:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="40db5cbc64f7481aa9f5274455b12bf9"><span data-offset-key="40db5cbc64f7481aa9f5274455b12bf9:0">Looked at a few puzzles related to the logical operators</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0"><span data-offset-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0:0">Looked at conversion functions such as </span><span data-offset-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0:1">`bool()`</span><span data-offset-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0:3">`int()`</span><span data-offset-key="4cfafd18963841d9b78e9e5cd4f27ab0:4"> to convert between boolean and integer data</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90dba7f4c58c46f88124f7bb5b855554"><span data-offset-key="90dba7f4c58c46f88124f7bb5b855554:0">Step 09:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35"><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:0">In this step, let’s look at two other important components of an </span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:2"> statement: </span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:3">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:5">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:6">. Let’s start with </span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:7">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="d226876eea9144c9b4d142a7d2788b35:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c79c0b3dfa3b4cf38918511adba1d79d"><span data-offset-key="c79c0b3dfa3b4cf38918511adba1d79d:0">**Snippet-01:**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31"><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:0">Consider a scenario where </span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:2"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:3">`2`</span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:4">. Let’s try to print a message </span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:5">`"i is even"`</span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:6"> if </span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:7">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:8"> is an even number. Otherwise, print </span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:9">`"i is odd"`</span><span data-offset-key="6af89a55e59a4353a2672813e137fa31:10">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d"><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:0">Earlier we wrote code along these lines: </span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:1">`if i % 2 == 0 : print("i is                                       even")`</span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:2">. However if this condition is not </span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:3">`True`</span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:4">, we would want to </span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:5">`print("i is odd")`</span><span data-offset-key="fe72679d09b84e0b8abde4ac47033b9d:6">. How do we accomplish that?</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 2    >>> if i%2 == 0:    ...   print("i is even");    ... else:    ...   print("i is odd");    ...    i is even

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69"><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:0">An </span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:1">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:2"> clause provides an alternative code body to execute, if the </span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:3">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:4"> condition is </span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:5">`False`</span><span data-offset-key="9717bdfc04504fa0a23bd7f7f5c89e69:6">.</span></span></span>

        >>> i = 3    >>> if i%2 == 0:    ...   print("i is even");    ... else:    ...   print("i is odd");    ...    i is odd

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c29edd3a06aa4a8ab6441934706e3183"><span data-offset-key="c29edd3a06aa4a8ab6441934706e3183:0">Let’s look at </span><span data-offset-key="c29edd3a06aa4a8ab6441934706e3183:1">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="c29edd3a06aa4a8ab6441934706e3183:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779"><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:0">We want to do something if </span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:1">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:2"> has value of </span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:3">`3`</span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:4">, and something totally different if </span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:5">`i`</span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:6"> has a value of </span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:7">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="c394f65f9a4a4cfc9b3630e74ec71779:8">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="11945747592b4f999374de265b394f13"><span data-offset-key="11945747592b4f999374de265b394f13:0">In short, we want to specify 2 alternatives to the </span><span data-offset-key="11945747592b4f999374de265b394f13:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="11945747592b4f999374de265b394f13:2"> condition. How can that be done?</span></span></span>

        >>> if i==1:    ...   print("i is 1")    ... elif i==2:    ...   print("i is 2")    ... else:    ...   print("i is not 1 or 2")    ...    i is not 1 or 2    >>>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4"><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:0">That’s where the </span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:1">**`elif`**</span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:2"> clause comes into the picture. The code in </span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:3">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:4"> is executed if the previous conditions are false and the current </span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:5">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="dc3baefee0fa4eb093e6d2ff6e4537c4:6"> condition is true.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="df05034218d4429887fcc79054202300"><span data-offset-key="df05034218d4429887fcc79054202300:0">**Summary**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="641a262a6fc5493a88f95751e7cb3ae5"><span data-offset-key="641a262a6fc5493a88f95751e7cb3ae5:0">In this step, we:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343"><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:0">Looked at two important components of the </span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:2"> statement: </span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:3">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:5">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="936ec3efcaf4492093c79e7794df0343:6">.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42"><span data-offset-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42:0">Understood that the </span><span data-offset-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42:1">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42:2"> clauses and the final </span><span data-offset-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42:3">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="252a61d92e74448a949a6d09775f5e42:4"> clause provide alternative conditions to check, when earlier if conditions are true.</span></span></span>

    number1 = int(input("Enter Number1: "))number2 = int(input("Enter Number2: "))​print("\n\n1 - Add")print("2 - Subtract")print("3 - Divide")print("4 - Multiply")​choice = int(input("Choose Operation: "))​# print(number1 + number2)# print(choice)if choice==1:    result = number1 + number2elif choice==2:    result = number1 - number2elif choice==3:    result = number1 / number2elif choice==4:    result = number1 * number2else:    result = "Invalid Choice"​print(result)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd"><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:0">In this step, let’s look at a few puzzles related to these </span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:1">`if`</span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:3">`elif`</span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:5">`else`</span><span data-offset-key="339a9ab4759d4a64a5c735f7442fd9bd:6"> clauses.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="16b01bf4245244cb81859f155acc081e"><span data-offset-key="16b01bf4245244cb81859f155acc081e:0">**Puzzle-01**</span></span></span>
